PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 1 of 210
Question ID: 651694
Which of the tools and techniques listed below is employed during the Plan Stakeholder
Engagement process?
- **A Decision tree analysis**
- **B Benchmarking**
- **C Process analysis**
- **D Hierarchical charts**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which technique helps the project team ensure that the project's stakeholder engagement efforts
compare favorably with other world-class efforts?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

There are six tools and techniques employed during the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering (e.g., benchmarking)
● Data analysis
● Decision making
● Data representation
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Decision tree analysis**
Incorrect. Decision tree analysis is a data analysis technique used during the Perform
Quantitative Risk Analysis process to support the selection of the best of several alternative
courses of action. It is not employed during the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **B Benchmarking**
Correct. Benchmarking is a data analysis tool used during the Plan Stakeholder
Engagement process to compare the results of the project's stakeholder analysis with
information obtained from other organizations or projects that are considered to be world
class.
- **C Process analysis**
Incorrect. Process analysis is a technique that is used during the Manage Quality process
to identify opportunities for process improvements. It is not used during the Plan
Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **D Hierarchical charts**
Incorrect. Hierarchical charts are employed during the Plan Resource Management
process to show positions, resources, relationships, and categories in a graphical,
top-down format. It is not listed in the PMBOK® Guide as a tool or technique that is used
during the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 526, 520
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 2 of 210
Question ID: 651685
Which of the following tools and techniques is used for both Control Resources and Manage
Quality?
- **A Negotiation**
- **B Influencing**
- **C Problem solving**
- **D Flow charts**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

With both Control Resources and Manage Quality, what could possibly go wrong?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the physical resources assigned and allocated to
the project are available as planned, as well as monitoring the planned versus actual utilization of
resources and performing corrective action as necessary. Control Resources has four tools and
techniques:
● Data analysis (alternatives analysis, cost-benefit analysis, performance reviews, trend
analysis)
● Problem solving
● Interpersonal and team skills (negotiation and influencing)
● Project management information systems (resource management or scheduling software)

---

Problem solving is only explicitly listed as a tool and technique for the Control Resources and
Manage Quality processes.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Negotiation**
Incorrect. Negotiation is an interpersonal and team skill that serves as a tool for the
Control Resources process, but not the Manage Quality process.
- **B Influencing**
Incorrect. Influencing is also an interpersonal and team skill that serves as a tool for the
Control Resources process, but not the Manage Quality process.
- **C Problem solving**
Correct. Problem solving may help solve problems that arise during the Control Resource
process, such as when machines used by another department are not released in time,
causing a delay for your project. In managing quality, problem solving may also solve
problems discovered in quality audits or issues where deliverables fail to pass quality
verification.
- **D Flow charts**
Incorrect. Flow charts are a data representation tool that is used for the Manage Quality
process, but not the Control Resources process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 356-357, 295
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 3 of 210
Question ID: 651573
Which of the following is an output of the Develop Schedule process?
- **A Activity list**
- **B Schedule data**
- **C Scope baseline**
- **D Resource breakdown structure**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Develop Schedule process generates a series of documents that support a schedule model
with planned dates for completing project activities.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Develop Schedule process has the following seven outputs:
● Schedule baseline
● Project schedule
● Schedule data
● Project calendars
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates

---

The Develop Schedule process is defined as "the process of analyzing activity sequences,
durations, resource requirements, and schedule constraints to create the project schedule model
for project execution and monitoring and controlling".

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Activity list**
Incorrect. An activity list is a project document that includes the schedule activities
required on the project. This document is an output from the Define Activities process and
is one of the inputs (not outputs) to the Develop Schedule process.
- **B Schedule data**
Correct. The schedule data is an output of the Develop Schedule process and is the
collection of information for describing and controlling the schedule. Therefore, schedule
data is the correct answer.
- **C Scope baseline**
Incorrect. While the scope baseline is an input to the Develop Schedule process, the
schedule baseline is an output of the process.
- **D Resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The resource breakdown structure is a hierarchical representation of resources
by category and type and is not listed in the PMBOK® Guide as an output of the Develop
Schedule process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 205, 220
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 4 of 210
Question ID: 651657
The Conduct Procurements process has six outputs, including:
● Selected sellers
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
● Organizational process assets updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
- **A Work performance reports**
- **B Enterprise environmental factors updates**
- **C Verified deliverables**
- **D Agreements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Conduct Procurements is the process of obtaining seller responses, selecting a seller, and
awarding a contract.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Conduct Procurements is the process of obtaining seller responses, selecting a seller, and
awarding a contract. The Conduct Procurements process has the following six outputs:
● Selected sellers
● Agreements

---

● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
● Organizational process assets updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance reports**
Incorrect. Work performance reports are not included in the PMBOK® Guide as an output
of the Conduct Procurements process.
- **B Enterprise environmental factors updates**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not include enterprise environmental factors updates
as an output of the Conduct Procurements process.
- **C Verified deliverables**
Incorrect. Verified deliverables are deliverables that have been checked for correctness,
and, therefore, are outputs of the Control Quality process, not the Conduct Procurements
process.
- **D Agreements**
Correct. An agreement is a contract between the buyer and seller for specified products.
Agreements are outputs of the Conduct Procurements process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 482, 489
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 5 of 210
Question ID: 651582
Which of the following is an output of the Determine Budget process?
- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
- **B Contracts**
- **C Cost baseline**
- **D Resource breakdown structure**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Determine Budget process aggregates the estimated costs of individual activities or work
packages to establish an authorized cost baseline.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Determine Budget process has the following outputs:
● Cost baseline
● Project funding requirements
● Project documents updates (cost estimates, project schedule, risk register)
Determine Budget is the process of aggregating the estimated costs of individual activities or
work packages to establish an authorized cost baseline.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. Requirements traceability matrix is an output of the Collect Requirements
process.
- **B Contracts**
Incorrect. Contracts are most often an output of procurement processes.
- **C Cost baseline**
Correct. The cost baseline is one of the more important outputs of the Determine Budget
process.
- **D Resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. Resource breakdown structure is an output of the Estimate Activity Resources
process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 248

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 6 of 210
Question ID: 651635
Which of the following is a tool and technique of the Identify Risks process?
- **A Project management information system**
- **B Trend analysis**
- **C Cost estimates**
- **D SWOT analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which choice can be used to identify individual risks?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Identify Risks is the process of identifying individual risks as well as sources of overall risk and
documenting their characteristics. This process employs six tools & techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering
● Data analysis (e.g., SWOT analysis)
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Prompt lists
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Project management information system**
Incorrect. The project management information system is a tool used during the Implement
Risk Response process. It is not a tool & technique in the PMBOK® Guide under the
Identify Risks process.
- **B Trend analysis**
Incorrect. Trend analysis is a technique employed in many processes to forecast future
performance based on past results. However, it is not used during the Identify Risks
process.
- **C Cost estimates**
Incorrect. Cost estimates are not a tool or technique but are instead an input to the Identify
Risks process.
- **D SWOT analysis**
Correct. SWOT (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, and Threats) analysis is a technique
used during the Identify Risks process to increase the breadth of identified risks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 409, 415

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Top of Form
Question 7 of 210
Question ID: 651642
Updates to which of the following are an output of the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis
process?
Top of Form
- **A Cost forecasts**
- **B Risk report**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Organizational process assets**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process focuses on determining overall risk to the
project's objectives.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process is where the effect of identified individual
project risks and other sources of uncertainty on overall project objectives is numerically
analyzed. This process has only one output, which is the project documents updates (e.g., the
risk report).

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Cost forecasts**
Incorrect. Cost forecasts are inputs of the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process.
However, updates to cost forecasts are neither inputs to nor outputs from this process.
- **B Risk report**
Correct. Updates to the risk report are the single output of the Perform Quantitative Risk
Analysis process, which analyzes the combined effect of individual project risks on overall
project objectives.
- **C Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is not updated by the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis
process, because the process focuses on overall project risk.
- **D Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Organizational process assets or OPAs are not updated by the Perform
Quantitative Risk Analysis process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 436
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 8 of 210
Question ID: 651695
Which of the following is not a tool and technique used during the Monitor Stakeholder
Engagement process?
- **A Root cause analysis**
- **B Presentations**
- **C Communication styles assessment**
- **D Cultural awareness**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which tool and technique seems out of place in the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Monitor Stakeholder Engagement is the process of monitoring project stakeholder relationships,
and tailoring strategies for engaging stakeholders through the modification of engagement
strategies and plans. This process uses six tools and techniques:
● Data analysis (including alternatives analysis, root cause analysis, and stakeholder
analysis)
● Decision making (including multicriteria decision analysis and voting)
● Data representation (e.g., the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix)
● Communication skills (including feedback and presentations)
● Interpersonal and team skills (including active listening, cultural awareness, leadership,
networking, and political awareness)
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Root cause analysis**
Incorrect. Root cause analysis is a technique used during the Monitor Stakeholder
Engagement process to determine the basic underlying reason that stakeholder engagement
is not having the planned effect.
- **B Presentations**
Incorrect. Presentations is a technique used during the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement
process to provide clear information to stakeholders.
- **C Communication styles assessment**
Correct. Communications styles assessment is a technique used during the Plan
Communications Management process to evaluate different communications styles and
identify the preferred communication method, format, and content for planned
communication activities.
- **D Cultural awareness**
Incorrect. Cultural awareness is a technique used during the Monitor Stakeholder
Engagement process to help the project manager plan communications based on the
cultural differences and requirements of stakeholders and team members.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 530, 375
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 9 of 210
Question ID: 651575
Which of the following is not a tool and technique of the Develop Schedule process?
- **A What-if scenario analysis**
- **B Critical path method**
- **C Resource optimization**
- **D Rolling wave planning**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the answers is a tool and technique typically used during the Define Activities process.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Develop Schedule process has the following eight tools and techniques:
● Schedule network analysis
● Critical path method
● Resource optimization
● Data analysis (e.g., what-if scenario analysis)
● Leads and lags
● Schedule compression
● Project management information system
● Agile release planning

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A What-if scenario analysis**
Incorrect. What-if scenario analysis is the process of evaluating scenarios to predict their
effect on project objectives. The outcome of the what-if scenario analysis can be used to
assess the feasibility of the project schedule under different conditions. Therefore, what-if
analysis is a data analysis tool and technique used during the Develop Schedule process.
- **B Critical path method**
Incorrect. The critical path method is a tool and technique used during the Develop
Schedule process to estimate the minimum project duration and determine the amount of
flexibility on the logical network paths within the schedule model.
- **C Resource optimization**
Incorrect. Resource optimization is used during the Develop Schedule process to adjust the
start and finish dates of activities to adjust planned resource use to be equal to or less than
resource availability. Therefore, resource optimization is a tool and technique used during
the Develop Schedule process.
- **D Rolling wave planning**
Correct. Rolling wave planning is an iterative planning technique in which the work to be
accomplished in the near term is planned in detail, while the work in the future is planned
at a higher level. Rolling wave planning is a tool and technique typically used during the
Define Activities process, and, therefore, the correct answer to the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 205, 185
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 10 of 210
Question ID: 651688
Which of the following is not a tool or technique used during the Monitor Communication
process?
- **A Observation/conversation**
- **B Communication methods**
- **C Interpersonal and team skills**
- **D Meetings**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is a tool and technique used in two of the three processes of Project
Communication Management.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Monitor Communications is the process of ensuring that the information needs of the project and
its stakeholders are met. This process has the following five tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Project management information system
● Data analysis
● Interpersonal and team skills (e.g., observations/conversation)
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Observation/conversation**
Incorrect. Observation/conversation is one of the interpersonal and team skills used during
the Monitor Communications process. Therefore, observation/conversation is a tool and
technique used during the process.
- **B Communication methods**
Correct. Communication methods are part of the tools and techniques used during the Plan
Communication Management and Manage Communications processes. However, the
PMBOK® Guide does not include communication methods among the tools and techniques
used in the Monitor Communications process.
- **C Interpersonal and team skills**
Incorrect. Interpersonal and team skills are part of the tools and techniques used during the
Monitor Communications process.
- **D Meetings**
Incorrect. The Monitor Communications process uses meetings as a tool and technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 388

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 11 of 210
Question ID: 651615
Which of the following is not an input to the Plan Communications Management process?
- **A Stakeholder register**
- **B Enterprise environmental factors (EEFs)**
- **C Performance reports**
- **D Organizational process assets (OPAs)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Plan Communications Management process is in the Planning Process Group.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Plan Communications Management is the process of developing an appropriate approach and
plan for project communication activities based on the information needs of each stakeholder or
group, available organizational assets, and the needs of the project. The Plan Communications
Management process has the following five inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., stakeholder register)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is an example of project documents that serve as inputs
to the Plan Communications Management process.
- **B Enterprise environmental factors (EEFs)**
Incorrect. EEFs are inputs to the Plan Communications Management process.
- **C Performance reports**
Correct. Performance reports are not an input to the Plan Communications Management
process; therefore, this answer is the correct.
- **D Organizational process assets (OPAs)**
Incorrect. OPAs are inputs to the Plan Communications Management process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 366

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 12 of 210
Question ID: 651606
Which of the following is not an input to the Develop Team process?
- **A Project team assignments**
- **B Issue log**
- **C Resource calendars**
- **D Resource management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Develop Team is the process of improving the competencies, team interaction, and the overall
team environment while Manage Team is the process of tracking team member performance,
providing feedback, resolving issues, and managing team changes.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Develop Team is the process of improving competences, team member interaction, and overall
team environment to enhance project performance. It has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan (resource management plan especially the team performance
assessment criteria, as well as guidance on rewards, feedback, training, and disciplinary
actions)
● Project documents (lessons learned register, project schedule, project team assignments,
resource calendars, team charter)
● Enterprise environmental factors (human resource management policies, team member
competencies, and geographic distribution)
● Organizational process assets (historical information and lessons learned repository)

---

The issue log is not an input project document for the Develop Team process, which is focused
on improving team competencies and interaction, and the overall team environment. Instead, the
Manage Team process, which is focused on oversight and issue resolution, uses the issue log as
an input for documenting and monitoring who is responsible for resolving issues by a target date.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project team assignments**
Incorrect. Project team assignments are included in the list of input project documents for
the Develop Team process.
- **B Issue log**
Correct. The issue log serves as an input project document for the Manage Team and
Control Resources process, not the Develop Team process.
- **C Resource calendars**
Incorrect. Resource calendars are included in the list of input project documents for the
Develop Team process.
- **D Resource management plan**
Incorrect. The resource management plan is a component of the project management plan
that serves as an input when developing the team.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 339-340, 347, 345
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 13 of 210
Question ID: 651548
All of the following are inputs to the Close Project or Phase process except:
- **A Project charter**
- **B Benefits management plan**
- **C Enterprise environmental factors**
- **D Procurement documentation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This input is used by most of the other processes, but not by the Close Project or Phase process.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Close Project or Phase is the process of finalizing all activities for the project, phase, or contract.
The Close Project or Phase process has the following eight inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Accepted deliverables
● Business documents
● Agreements
● Procurement documentation
● Organizational process assets

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter documents the project success criteria, the approval
requirements, and who will sign off on the project. Therefore, the project charter is an input
to the Close Project or Phase process.
- **B Benefits management plan**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan outlines the target benefits of the project and is
used to measure whether the benefits of the project were achieved as planned. Therefore,
the benefits management plan is an input to the Close Project or Phase process.
- **C Enterprise environmental factors**
Correct. While enterprise environmental factors (EEFs) are inputs to numerous project
management processes, they are not listed as inputs to the Close Project or Phase process
in the PMBOK® Guide. Therefore, EEFs is the correct answer.
- **D Procurement documentation**
Incorrect. The Close Project or Phase process includes confirmation that the contract
closure has been done satisfactorily; therefore, procurement documentation is required as
an input to this process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 121
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 14 of 210
Question ID: 651668
All of the following are tools and techniques used in the Manage Project Knowledge process
except:
- **A Facilitation**
- **B Political awareness**
- **C Brainstorming**
- **D Networking**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Data gathering is not a tool or technique used in the Manage Project Knowledge process.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Manage Project Knowledge process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Knowledge management
● Information management
● Interpersonal and team skills (e.g., facilitation, networking, political awareness)
Manage Project Knowledge is the process of using existing knowledge and creating new
knowledge to achieve the project's objectives and contribute to organizational learning.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Facilitation**
Incorrect. Facilitation is an example of an interpersonal and team skill that helps
effectively guide a group to a successful solution. Facilitation is a tool and technique used
in the Manage Project Knowledge process.
- **B Political awareness**
Incorrect. Political awareness is an example of an interpersonal and team skill that helps
the project manager plan communications based on the organization's political
environment. Political awareness is a tool and technique used in the Manage Project
Knowledge process.
- **C Brainstorming**
Correct. Brainstorming is an example of a data gathering technique which is not one of the
tools and techniques used in the Manage Project Knowledge process, and, therefore, the
correct answer to the question asked.
- **D Networking**
Incorrect. Networking is an example of an interpersonal and team skill that creates the
conditions for stakeholders to share knowledge. Networking is a tool and technique used in
the Manage Project Knowledge process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 98, 104

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Question 15 of 210
Question ID: 651655
The Conduct Procurements process has six inputs, including:
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Procurement documentation
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
Which of the following inputs is missing from the list?
- **A Procurement statement of work**
- **B Source selection criteria**
- **C Seller proposals**
- **D Project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Two of the available options are examples of procurement documentation, and, therefore, are on
the list in the question.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Conduct Procurements is the process of obtaining seller responses, selecting a seller, and
awarding a contract. The Conduct Procurements process has the following six inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents

---

● Procurement documentation (e.g., source selection criteria, procurement statement of
work)
● Seller proposals
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Procurement statement of work**
Incorrect. The procurement statement of work is an example of procurement
documentation, an input to the Conduct Procurements process. Procurement documentation
is on the list in the question; therefore, this answer is not correct.
- **B Source selection criteria**
Incorrect. Source selection criteria is an example of procurement documentation used as an
input to the Conduct Procurements process. The list in the question contains procurement
documentation.
- **C Seller proposals**
Correct. Seller proposals are used to select the vendors that will be used on the project.
Seller proposals are inputs to the Conduct Procurements process and are missing from the
list in the question.
- **D Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is not an input to the Conduct Procurements process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 482, 486

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 16 of 210
Question ID: 651676
Which of the following is not an input to the Plan Schedule Management process?
- **A Expert judgment**
- **B Scope management plan**
- **C Development approach**
- **D Project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the answers is a tool and technique.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Plan Schedule Management process has the following four inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan (e.g., scope management plan, development approach)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Expert judgment**
Correct. Expert judgment is a tool and technique used in the Plan Schedule Management
process, not an input to the process.
- **B Scope management plan**
Incorrect. The scope management plan is a component of the project management plan
which describes how the scope will be defined and developed. How the scope is defined and
developed will influence how the schedule is developed; therefore, the scope management
plan is an input to the Plan Schedule Management process.
- **C Development approach**
Incorrect. The product development approach will help define the scheduling approach,
estimating techniques, and scheduling tools used during the Plan Schedule Management
process. As a component of the project management plan, the development approach is an
input to the process.
- **D Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter defines the summary milestone schedule that will influence
the management of the project schedule, and is, therefore, an input to the Plan Schedule
Management process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 179, 180

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 17 of 210
Question ID: 651547
Which of the following is a tool or technique used in the Perform Integrated Change Control
process?
- **A Conflict management**
- **B Project management information system**
- **C Change requests**
- **D Multicriteria decision analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Perform Integrated Change Control process involves deciding whether to approve changes
to the project.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Perform Integrated Change Control is the process of reviewing all change requests; approving
changes and managing changes to deliverables, organizational process assets, project documents,
and the project management plan; and communicating the decisions. The Perform Integrated
Change Control process has the following five tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Change control tools
● Data analysis
● Decision making (e.g., multicriteria decision analysis)
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Conflict management**
Incorrect. Conflict management is an example of the interpersonal and team skills tool and
technique, which is not used in the Perform Integrated Change Control process.
- **B Project management information system**
Incorrect. The project management information system is a tool that is used in several
processes; however, the Perform Integrated Change Control process is not one of them.
- **C Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are usually an input or an output, but not a tool or technique. In
the Perform Integrated Change Control process, change requests are inputs to the process.
- **D Multicriteria decision analysis**
Correct. The decision-making tool and technique, of which multicriteria decision analysis
is an example, is used in the Perform Integrated Change Control process. Multicriteria
decision analysis uses a decision matrix to provide a systematic analytical approach to
evaluate the requested changes according to a set of predefined criteria.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 113, 119
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 18 of 210
Question ID: 651630
Which of the following is not an input to the Plan Risk Responses process?
- **A Risk register**
- **B Scope baseline**
- **C Stakeholder register**
- **D Cost baseline**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer has little or no effect on risk response planning?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Plan Risk Responses is the process of developing options, selecting strategies, and agreeing on
actions to address overall project risk exposure, as well as to treat individual project risks. This
process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan (including the risk management plan, the resource management
plan, and the cost baseline)
● Project documents (including the lessons learned register, the project schedule, project
team assignments, resource calendars, the risk register, the risk report, and the
stakeholder register)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is an input to the Plan Risk Responses process that contains
details of individual project risks that require risk responses.
- **B Scope baseline**
Correct. The scope baseline is not an input to the Plan Risk Responses process.
- **C Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is an input to the Plan Risk Responses process, used to
identify potential owners for risk responses.
- **D Cost baseline**
Incorrect. The cost baseline is an input to the Plan Risk Responses process that contains
information on the contingency fund allocated to respond to risks.

Question 19 of 210
Question ID: 651666
All of the following are inputs to the Manage Project Knowledge process except:
- **A Project charter**
- **B Lessons learned register**
- **C Deliverables**
- **D Project team assignments**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Only one answer is never an input in the Executing Process Group.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Manage Project Knowledge process has the following five inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., lessons learned register, project team assignments)
● Deliverables
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
The Manage Project Knowledge is the process of using existing knowledge and creating new
knowledge to achieve the project's objectives and contribute to organizational learning./p>

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter**
Correct. The project charter is not an input to the Manage Project Knowledge process.
- **B Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register provides information on effective practices in
knowledge management and is an input to the Manage Project Knowledge process.
- **C Deliverables**
Incorrect. Deliverables are typically tangible components completed to meet the project
objectives and can include components of the project management plan. Deliverables are
inputs to the Manage Project Knowledge process.
- **D Project team assignments**
Incorrect. Project team assignments provide information on the type of competencies and
experience available in the project and the knowledge that may be missing. Therefore,
project team assignments are inputs to the Manage Project Knowledge process.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 20 of 210
Question ID: 651568
Which of the following is not a tool or technique of the Estimate Activity Resources process?
- **A Analogous estimating**
- **B Parametric estimating**
- **C Three-point estimating**
- **D Bottom-up estimating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Most estimating techniques create single-point estimates which are appropriate for not only
human resources and discrete physical supplies, but also for activity durations and costs.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Estimate Activity Resources is the process of estimating team resources and the type and
quantities of material, equipment, and supplies necessary to perform project work. This process
has the following seven tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Bottom-up estimating
● Analogous estimating
● Parametric estimating
● Data analysis
● Project management information systems (PMIS)
● Meetings

---

Using a range to account for uncertainty and risk, the three-point estimating technique is used
only to estimate activity durations and costs. All the other estimating techniques create
single-point estimates, which are appropriate for not only activity duration and cost but also
human resources and discrete physical supplies.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Analogous estimating**
Incorrect. Analogous estimating uses information from a previous similar project to
forecast schedule activity durations, costs, and activity resources. It is a technique used in
the Estimate Activity Resources process.
- **B Parametric estimating**
Incorrect. Parametric estimating uses an algorithm or statistical relationship between
historical data and project parameters to forecast schedule activity durations, costs, and
activity resources. It is a technique used in the Estimate Activity Resources process.
- **C Three-point estimating**
Correct. Three-point estimating uses a triangular distribution or weighted beta distribution
that averages the optimistic, pessimistic, and most likely estimates to forecast a range of
schedule activity durations and costs, but not activity resources.
- **D Bottom-up estimating**
Incorrect. Bottom-up estimating breaks down the project to the detailed activity level then
aggregates the estimates to forecast the schedule activity durations, costs, and activity
resources for the work packages, control accounts, and summary project level. It is a
technique used in the Estimate Activity Resources process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 324-325, 691-694, 195, 240
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 21 of 210
Question ID: 651586
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Control Costs process?
- **A Project funding requirements**
- **B Communication methods**
- **C Project management plan**
- **D To-complete performance index**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Control Costs process enables monitoring the status of the project to update the project
budget and managing changes to the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Control Costs process has the following tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Earned value management (EVM)
● Variance analysis
● Trend analysis
● Reserve analysis
● To-complete performance index (TCPI)
● Project management information systems

---

Control Costs is the process of monitoring the status of the project to update the project costs and
manage changes to the cost baseline.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project funding requirements**
Incorrect. Project funding requirements are not classified as a tool or technique used in the
Control Costs process; they are inputs.
- **B Communication methods**
Incorrect. Communication methods are not tools and techniques used in the Control Costs
process.
- **C Project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan is an input but not a tool or technique used in the
Control Costs process.
- **D To-complete performance index**
Correct. The to-complete performance index is a tool and technique used in the Control
Costs process. The TCPI is used to forecast how reasonable the plans are to meet either the
EAC or BAC.

**Reference:**

Question 22 of 210
Question ID: 651622
Which input of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process describes the methods, formats,
and technologies used to communicate with stakeholders?
- **A Work performance reports**
- **B Communications management plan**
- **C Lessons learned register**
- **D Stakeholder engagement plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which option provides comprehensive communications details?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the process of communicating and working with
stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations, address issues, and foster appropriate
stakeholder involvement. The process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan (including the communications management plan,
stakeholder engagement plan, the risk management plan, the and the change management
plan)
● Project documents (including the change log, the issue log, the lessons learned register,
and the stakeholder register)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance reports**
Incorrect. Work performance reports are not inputs of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement
process.
- **B Communications management plan**
Correct. The communications management plan provides all the communications details
for stakeholder engagement, including methods, formats, and technologies.
- **C Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is an input to the Manage Stakeholder Engagement
process. Although the lessons learned register might contain information on improvements
to stakeholder communications, the register does not contain all the details on
communications methods, formats, and technologies.
- **D Stakeholder engagement plan**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement plan is an input to the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process. While the stakeholder engagement plan contains considerable
information concerning stakeholder communications, the communications management
plan contains the details on communications methods, formats, and technologies.

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 23 of 210
Question ID: 651511
Which of the following statements is false?
- **A The Estimate Activity Durations process uses both decision-making techniques and**
reserve analysis to estimate durations.
- **B The Estimate Activity Durations process uses the following organizational process assets:**
historical duration information, scheduling methodology, and published commercial information.
- **C The risk register provides a list of risks, the results of risk analysis, and risk response**
planning to the Estimate Activity Durations process as inputs.
- **D The Estimate Activity Durations process can produce updates to the activity attributes.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Look for an enterprise environmental factor that is being improperly identified.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Estimate Activity Durations process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Enterprise environmental factors (e.g., published commercial information)
● Organizational process assets (e.g., historical information, scheduling methodology)
It is in this process that the number of work periods needed to complete individual activities with
the estimated resources is estimated.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The Estimate Activity Durations process uses both decision-making techniques and**
reserve analysis to estimate durations.
Incorrect. This statement is true. Both decision-making techniques and reserve analysis are
used as tools and techniques in the Estimate Activity Durations process.
- **B The Estimate Activity Durations process uses the following organizational process assets:**
historical duration information, scheduling methodology, and published commercial information.
Correct. This statement is false. While historical duration information and scheduling
methodology are examples of organizational process assets, published commercial
information is an example of enterprise environmental factors.
- **C The risk register provides a list of risks, the results of risk analysis, and risk response**
planning to the Estimate Activity Durations process as inputs.
Incorrect. This statement is true. A list of risks, the results of risk analysis and risk response
planning is provided by the risk register as an input to the Estimate Activity Durations
process.
- **D The Estimate Activity Durations process can produce updates to the activity attributes.**
Incorrect. This statement is true. The activity attributes may be updated as a result of
estimating activity durations and are outputs of the Estimate Activity Durations process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 195, 199

Question 24 of 210
Question ID: 651675
Which of the following is not a tool or technique used in the Plan Schedule Management
process?
- **A Alternatives analysis**
- **B Meetings**
- **C Expert judgment**
- **D Multicriteria decision analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Data analysis is one of the tools and techniques used in the Plan Schedule Management process.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Plan Schedule Management process has the following three tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data analysis (e.g., alternatives analysis)
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Alternatives analysis**
Incorrect. Alternatives analysis is a data analysis technique that can be used in the Plan
Schedule Management process for determining which schedule methodology to use, how
detailed the schedule needs to be, or the duration of waves for rolling wave planning.
Therefore, alternatives analysis is not the correct answer.
- **B Meetings**
Incorrect. Project teams may hold planning meetings to develop the schedule management
plan. Therefore, it is true that meetings 'are' a tool or technique used in the Plan Schedule
Management process.
- **C Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expertise from individuals with specialized knowledge in schedule development,
scheduling methodologies, and scheduling software should be considered during the Plan
Schedule Management process. Therefore, expert judgment is a tool and technique used in
the process and is not the correct answer.
- **D Multicriteria decision analysis**
Correct. Multicriteria decision analysis is an example of a decision-making tool and
technique. The PMBOK® Guide does not include decision-making as a tool and technique
used in the Plan Schedule Management process making this option the best answer to the
question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 179, 181

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 25 of 210
Question ID: 651637
Which of the following is a tool and technique of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process?
- **A Probability and impact matrix**
- **B Reserve analysis**
- **C Strategies for threats**
- **D Schedule network analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is the process of prioritizing risks for further analysis or
action by assessing and combining their probability of occurrence and impact.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is the process of prioritizing individual project risks for
further analysis or action by assessing their probability of occurrence and impact as well as other
characteristics. This process has seven tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering
● Data analysis
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Risk categorization
● Data representation (e.g., probability and impact matrix)
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Probability and impact matrix**
Correct. The probability and impact matrix is a tool used in the Perform Qualitative Risk
Analysis process to assess the priority of individual risks.
- **B Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis is not a tool or technique of the Perform Qualitative Risk
Analysis process. It is a technique used in the Estimate Costs and Determine Budget
processes to estimate contingency and management reserves. It is also used during the
Control Costs and Monitor Risks processes to monitor reserves and ensure that they are
adequate for the remaining risks. Additionally, reserve analysis is used during the Estimate
Activity Durations process to determine the need for schedule reserves.
- **C Strategies for threats**
Incorrect. Strategies for threats is a tool used in the Plan Risk Responses process to provide
options for dealing with threats. These strategies include escalation, avoidance, and
mitigation. These strategies are not tools or techniques of the Perform Qualitative Risk
Analysis process.
- **D Schedule network analysis**
Incorrect. Schedule network analysis is a technique used during the Develop Schedule
process to generate the project schedule model. Schedule network analysis is not a tool or
technique of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 419, 425
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 26 of 210
Question ID: 651564
The Sequence Activities process has four tools and techniques, including:
● Precedence diagramming method (PDM)
● Dependency determination and integration
● Project management information system
Which of the following tools and techniques is missing from the list?
- **A Expert judgment**
- **B Project schedule network diagrams**
- **C Published estimating data**
- **D Leads and lags**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Sequence Activities is the process of identifying and documenting relationships among the
project activities.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Sequence Activities process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Precedence diagramming method (PDM)
● Dependency determination and integration
● Leads and lags

---

● Project management information system
This process is where the relationships among the project activities is identified and documented.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Expert judgment**
Incorrect. While expert judgment is a tool and technique for numerous project management
processes, it is not listed as a tool and technique for the Sequence Activities process in the
PMBOK® Guide. Therefore, expert judgment is an incorrect answer.
- **B Project schedule network diagrams**
Incorrect. Project schedule network diagrams are outputs of the Sequence Activities
process, not a tool and technique.
- **C Published estimating data**
Incorrect. Published estimating data is an example of enterprise environmental factors,
which are inputs, not a tool and technique.
- **D Leads and lags**
Correct. A lead is the amount of time a successor activity can be advanced with respect to a
predecessor activity. A lag is the amount of time a successor activity will be delayed with
respect to a predecessor activity. Leads and lags are techniques used in the Sequence
Activities process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 187, 192-193

Question 27 of 210
Question ID: 626025
There was a delay in the delivery of materials and equipment that have been purchased from a
supplier.
Where should you look for guidance on resolving this issue?
Top of Form
- **A Resource management plan and procurement contracts**
- **B Resource requirements and policies for resource control**
- **C Issue escalation procedures and project schedule**
- **D Work performance data and lessons learned repository**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What answer choice describes inputs to the Control Resources process that would guide you in
resolving supplier issues?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests you are performing the Control Resources process. Control Resources is
the process of ensuring that the physical resources assigned and allocated to the project are
available as planned, as well as monitoring the planned versus actual utilization of resources and
taking actions as necessary. While all answer choices can be valid inputs to the Control

---

Resources process, only the resource management plan and procurement contracts specify
actions that should be taken while resolving issues with suppliers.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Resource management plan and procurement contracts**
Correct. Procurement contracts are agreements that may define options for resolving issues
with specific sellers. The resource management plan usually has resource control guidance
on ensuring adequate physical resources are available as needed.
- **B Resource requirements and policies for resource control**
Incorrect. While policies for resource control are organizational process assets that may
provide guidance for resolving issues with suppliers, resource requirements only identify
the needed resources and no guidance for how to address supplier's delays in the delivery
of materials and equipment.
- **C Issue escalation procedures and project schedule**
Incorrect. Escalation procedures are organizational process assets that may provide
guidance for controlling resources activity. However, the project schedule would only show
when resources are needed at what locations but does not provide the appropriate guidance
for the issue in question.
- **D Work performance data and lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. Both work performance information and the lessons learned repository are valid
inputs to the Control Resource process described in the scenario. While the lessons learned
repository may have information on how issues with suppliers have been addressed in past
projects, work performance data contains not contextualized data on project status which
unlikely be helpful in addressing the issue at hand.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 354-355
Bottom of Form

Question 28 of 210
Question ID: 651556
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Validate Scope process?
Top of Form
- **A Decomposition**
- **B Expert judgment**
- **C Inspection**
- **D Change control meetings**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think about what activities may be involved in the Validate Scope process to formalize
acceptance of the completed project deliverables.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

With only two tools and techniques, namely inspection and decision making, the Validate Scope
process focuses on examining deliverables to decide whether the work meets the requirements
and acceptance criteria.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Decomposition**
Incorrect. Decomposition is a key tool of the Create WBS and Define Activities processes,
but not the Validate Scope process.
- **B Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is a tool that is used for planning scope management, collecting
requirements, defining the scope, and creating the WBS. In contrast, the Validate Scope
process should rely on the stakeholder’s decision to formally accept the verified
deliverables based on inspection.
- **C Inspection**
Correct. The Validate Scope process uses inspection, which includes activities to measure,
examine, and validate deliverables to determine whether the work meets the stakeholder’s
requirements and acceptance criteria.
- **D Change control meetings**
Incorrect. Change requests may be an output of the Validate Scope process if defect repair
merits a change to a baseline. Change control meetings are held to review, approve, reject,
and defer change requests, so meetings serve as a tool in the Perform Integrated Change
Control process, not the Validate Scope process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166
Bottom of Form

Question 29 of 210
Question ID: 651605
Which of the following is an output of the Develop Team process?
- **A Organizational process assets**
- **B Work performance information**
- **C Team performance assessments**
- **D Training**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Develop Team is the process of improving the competencies, team interaction, and the overall
team environment. Some of the choices are not outputs but inputs or tools.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Develop Team is the process of improving competences, team member interaction, and overall
team environment to enhance project performance. The Develop Project Team process has the
following six outputs:
● Team performance assessments (effectiveness in performing assignments, working as a
team, reducing turnover, open sharing and helping one another)
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (resource management plan)
● Project document updates (lessons learned register, project schedule, project team
assignments, resource calendars, team charter)
● Enterprise environmental factors updates (employee development plan records and skill
assessments)

---

● Organizational process assets updates (training requirements and personnel assessments)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. OPAs are used as inputs, not outputs. For team development, the relevant output
is organizational process asset updates, where you update records on training requirements
and personnel assessments. This process does have organizational process assets updates
as outputs.
- **B Work performance information**
Incorrect. Work performance information serves as an output for the Control Resources
process, not Develop Team process.
- **C Team performance assessments**
Correct. As project team development efforts such as training, team building, and
colocation are implemented, the project management team makes formal or informal
assessments of the project team’s effectiveness.
- **D Training**
Incorrect. Training is a tool and technique for the Develop Team process, not an output.

Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 343-344

Question ID: 651527
Which of the following is not an input used in the same process that uses work performance

Think of the activities performed as part of Monitor and Control Project Work.

● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., schedule forecasts, costs forecasts, quality reports)
● Work performance information

● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
Monitor and Control Project Work is the process of tracking, reviewing, and reporting overall
progress to meet the performance objectives defined in the project management plan. It is helpful

---

to note that work performance information is an input only to the Monitor and Control Project

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 31 of 210
Question ID: 651620
Which of the following is not a tool and technique of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement
process?
- **A Observation/conversation**
- **B Communication skills**
- **C Independent estimates**
- **D Ground rules**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the choices does not significantly contribute to the process of communicating and
working with stakeholders to meet their needs and addressing issues.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the process of communicating and working with
stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations, address issues, and foster appropriate
stakeholder involvement. This process has the following five tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Communication skills (e.g., feedback)
● Interpersonal and team skills (including conflict management, cultural awareness,
negotiation, observation/conversation, and political awareness)
● Ground rules
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Observation/conversation**
Incorrect. Observation/conversation is one of a variety of interpersonal and team skills
used during the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process to stay in touch with the work
and attitudes of the project team members and other stakeholders.
- **B Communication skills**
Incorrect. Communications skills (e.g. feedback) is a tool & technique of the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement process used to assist in understanding stakeholder reaction to
the various project activities and key decisions.
- **C Independent estimates**
Correct. Independent estimates, the process of using a third party to obtain and analyze
information to support the prediction of cost, schedule, etc., are not a tool and technique
used during the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **D Ground rules**
Incorrect. Ground rules is a tool and technique used during the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process to set the expected behavior for project team members and other
stakeholders regarding stakeholder engagement.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 523, 708

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 32 of 210
Question ID: 651525
Approved change requests are a result of which of the following processes?
- **A Direct and Manage Project Work**
- **B Control Quality**
- **C Control Procurements**
- **D Perform Integrated Change Control**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which process reviews all change requests?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Perform Integrated Change Control is the process of reviewing all change requests; approving
changes and managing changes to deliverables, organizational process assets, project documents,
and the project management plan; and communicating the decisions. The Perform Integrated
Change Control process has the following three outputs:
● Approved change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project document updates

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Direct and Manage Project Work**
Incorrect. Approved change requests are inputs, not outputs of the Direct and Manage
Project Work process.
- **B Control Quality**
Incorrect. Approved change requests are inputs, not outputs of the Control Quality process.
- **C Control Procurements**
Incorrect. Approved change requests are inputs, not outputs of the Control Procurements
process.
- **D Perform Integrated Change Control**
Correct. Approved change requests are outputs of the Perform Integrated Change Control
process, and is the only process that has approved change requests as outputs.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 113, 120

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 33 of 210
Question ID: 651567
Which of the following is an output of the Estimate Activity Resources process?
- **A Project team assignments**
- **B Activity duration estimates**
- **C Scope baseline**
- **D Resource breakdown structure**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Keep in mind that Estimate Activity Resources is a process in the Planning Process Group,
where you estimate the type and quantities of material, people, equipment, or supplies required
to perform each activity.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Estimate Activity Resources is the process of estimating team resources and the type and
quantities of material, equipment, and supplies necessary to perform project work. This process
has four outputs:
● Resource requirements
● Basis of estimates
● Resource breakdown structure by category (labor, material, equipment, and supplies)
and type (experience, education, certifications, and skills)
● Project documents updates

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project team assignments**
Incorrect. Project team assignments are outputs of the Acquire Resources process, which
takes place during the Executing Process Group. The Estimate Activity Resources process
takes place in Planning. Project team assignments are not outputs of the Estimate Activity
Resources process.
- **B Activity duration estimates**
Incorrect. The estimates of activity durations are outputs of Estimate Activity Durations, a
Project Schedule Management process. The process in question is Estimate Activity
Resources, which belongs to the Project Resource Management Knowledge Area, where the
corresponding output is "resource requirements". Therefore, activity duration estimates are
not outputs of the Estimate Activity Resources process.
- **C Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The scope baseline is an output of the Create WBS process in the Project Scope
Management Knowledge Area. For the Estimate Activity Resources process, the scope
baseline serves as an input and is a project management plan component; however, the
scope baseline is not an output of the Estimate Activity Resources process.
- **D Resource breakdown structure**
Correct. The resource breakdown structure is one of the principal outputs of the Estimate
Activity Resources process, which is the first process taking place after the resource
management plan is created.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 325-327

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 34 of 210
Question ID: 651600
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Plan Resource Management process?
- **A Requirements documentation**
- **B Organizational governance framework**
- **C Organization charts**
- **D Team charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Activities and tools in the Plan Resource Management process should establish the approach and
level of management effort needed for managing project resources based on the type and
complexity of the project.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Plan Resource Management is the process of defining how to estimate, acquire, manage, and
utilize physical and team resources. The Plan Resource Management process has the following
four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data representation (hierarchical charts, responsibility assignment matrix, and
text-oriented formats)
● Organizational theory
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation is a project document that serves not as a tool and
technique, but as an input to the Plan Resource Management process. The type and amount
of resources needed may dictate how the resources should be managed.
- **B Organizational governance framework**
Incorrect. Projects operate within the constraints of responsibility, accountability, and
authority imposed by the organizational governance framework. However, the framework is
not to be confused with organizational theory, which is explicitly listed as a tool for the
Plan Resource Management process.
- **C Organization charts**
Correct. Organization charts are a hierarchical structure used to show positions and
relationships graphically. Such charts comprise one of several data representation
techniques that serve as a tool and technique for the Plan Resource Management process.
- **D Team charter**
Incorrect. The team charter is not a tool or technique of Plan Resource Management
process, but an output that establishes the team values, agreements, and operating
guidelines for the team. It may include communication guidelines, decision-making criteria
and process, conflict resolution process, meeting guidelines, and team agreements.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 315-318

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 35 of 210
Question ID: 651681
Decomposition is a tool and technique of which two processes?
Top of Form
- **A Create WBS and Estimate Activity Resources**
- **B Create WBS and Plan Risk Management**
- **C Define Scope and Create WBS**
- **D Create WBS and Define Activities**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The results of your first decomposition feed directly into another knowledge area explicitly for
another round of decomposition.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Decomposition is a technique used for dividing and subdividing the project scope and project
deliverables into smaller, more manageable parts. It is explicitly listed as a tool and technique for
both the Create WBS and the Define Activities processes.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Create WBS and Estimate Activity Resources**
Incorrect. Certainly, decomposition is a key tool for the Create WBS process.
Decomposition might also be helpful to form a resource breakdown structure. However, the
Estimate Activity Resources process does not explicitly list decomposition as a tool and
technique, instead focusing on estimation and analysis techniques.
- **B Create WBS and Plan Risk Management**
Incorrect. Again, the tools and techniques for the Create WBS process include
decomposition. Although decomposition may be helpful to form a risk breakdown structure,
the Plan Risk Management process does not explicitly list decomposition as a tool and
technique.
- **C Define Scope and Create WBS**
Incorrect. Again, the Create WBS process uses decomposition as a tool to break down the
work products by categories. However, the Define Scope process does not explicitly list
decomposition as a tool and technique, instead focusing on judgment, data analysis,
decision making, team skills (facilitation), and product analysis.
- **D Create WBS and Define Activities**
Correct. Both the Create WBS and Define Activities processes explicitly list decomposition
as a tool and technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 156, 185

Question 36 of 210
Question ID: 651555
The outputs of the Create WBS process include the project scope statement, the work package(s),
the planning package(s), the WBS dictionary, and updates to the assumption log and the
requirements documentation.
Which of the following outputs is missing from this list?
- **A Work breakdown structure**
- **B Project management plan**
- **C Organizational process assets updates**
- **D Duration estimates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think about what process would produce each given choice as an output. Only one choice is an
output of the Create WBS process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Create WBS process subdivides the project deliverables and project work into smaller, more
manageable components. It has the following two outputs:
● The project scope baseline includes the project scope statement, the work package(s), the
planning package(s), the work breakdown structure, and the WBS dictionary
● The updates to project documents including the assumption log and the requirements
documentation.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work breakdown structure**
Correct. The main output of the Create WBS process is the work breakdown structure.
- **B Project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan is an input to the Create WBS process, not an
output.
- **C Organizational process assets updates**
Incorrect. You may update OPAs such as databases for issue and defect management,
performance measurement, staff training and assessment, correspondence, and qualified
sellers in the Direct and Manage Project Work, Manage Project Knowledge, Close Project
or Phase, Acquire Resources, Develop Team, Manage Communications, Monitor Risks,
Plan Procurement Management and Control Procurements processes. However, OPA
updates are not outputs for the Create WBS process.
- **D Duration estimates**
Incorrect. Duration estimates are considered a project document, and the process, where
duration estimates serve as outputs is the Estimate Activity Durations process, part of the
Schedule Management Knowledge Area.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 161-162

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 37 of 210
Question ID: 651581
Which of the following is not a tool or technique of the Estimate Costs process?
- **A Stakeholder analysis**
- **B Project management information systems**
- **C Cost of quality**
- **D Analogous estimating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Estimate Costs process develops an approximation of the monetary resources needed to
complete project activities.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Estimate Costs is the process of developing an approximation of the monetary resources needed
to complete project work. This process has the following ten tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Analogous estimating
● Parametric estimating
● Bottom-up estimating
● Three-point estimates
● Alternatives analysis
● Reserve analysis
● Cost of quality
● Project management information systems

---

● Decision making

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Stakeholder analysis**
Correct. Stakeholder analysis is not a tool or technique used in the Estimate Costs process.
Stakeholder analysis is a tool and techniques on some risk and stakeholder processes.
- **B Project management information systems**
Incorrect. A project management information system is a tool and technique in the Estimate
Costs process. A PMIS can include spreadsheets, simulation software, and statistical
analysis tools to assist with cost estimating.
- **C Cost of quality**
Incorrect. Cost of quality is tool and technique on the Estimate Costs process. Part of data
analysis along with alternatives and reserves analysis.
- **D Analogous estimating**
Incorrect. Analogous estimating is tool and technique on the Estimate Costs process.
Analogous cost estimating uses values, or attributes, of a previous project that are similar
to the current project. Comparison of these project values, or attributes, becomes the basis
for estimating the same parameter or measurement for the current project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 240
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 38 of 210
Question ID: 651645
The Plan Risk Responses process has three outputs, including:
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
- **B Schedule data**
- **C Change requests**
- **D Risk categorization**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How will this process deal with updates to cost or schedule baselines driven by planned risk
responses?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Plan Risk Responses is the process of developing options, selecting strategies, and agreeing on
actions to address overall project risk exposure, as well as to treat individual project risks. It has
the following three outputs:
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (including the schedule, cost, quality, resource, and
procurement management plans, and the scope, schedule, and cost baselines)

---

● Project documents updates (including the assumption log, cost forecasts, the lessons
learned register, the project schedule, project team assignments, the risk register, and the
risk report)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is an output of the Collect Requirements
process that links product requirements to the deliverables that satisfy them. It is not an
output of the Plan Risk Responses process.
- **B Schedule data**
Incorrect. Schedule data is an output of the Develop Schedule process that is the collection
of information for describing and controlling the schedule. It is not an output of the Plan
Risk Responses process.
- **C Change requests**
Correct. Change requests are outputs of the Plan Risk Responses process that enable
changes to the cost baseline, schedule baseline, or other components of the project
management plan.
- **D Risk categorization**
Incorrect. Risk categorization is not an output. It is a technique used during the Perform
Qualitative Risk Analysis process to group risks into useful categories such as the area of
the project affected, project phase, or sources.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 437, 447
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
