PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 39 of 210
Question ID: 651648
Which of the following is not an output of the Monitor Risks process?
- **A Change requests**
- **B Risk reviews**
- **C Risk report updates**
- **D Issue log updates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The key is to differentiate between inputs, outputs, and tools & techniques.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Monitor Risks is the process of monitoring the implementation of agreed-upon risk response
plans, tracking identified risks, identifying and analyzing new risks, and evaluating risk process
effectiveness throughout the project. This process has five outputs, including:
● Work performance information
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (any component)
● Project documents updates (including the assumption log, the issue log, the lessons
learned register, the risk register, and the risk report)
● Organizational process assets updates

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are outputs of the Monitor Risks process that enable
modifications to the cost or schedule baselines or other components of the project
management plan.
- **B Risk reviews**
Correct. Risk reviews are meetings used to examine and document the effectiveness of risk
responses during the Monitor Risks process. They are a type of tool/technique and are not
outputs.
- **C Risk report updates**
Incorrect. The risk report can be updated as a result of carrying out the Monitor Risks
process to reflect the current status of major individual project risks and the current level of
overall project risk.
- **D Issue log updates**
Incorrect. Issue log updates are an output of the Monitor Risks process. The issue log can
be updated with the new issues that have arisen during the process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 453, 457

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 40 of 210
Question ID: 651639
Which output of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process includes a prioritized list of all
identified risks and a summary conclusion?
- **A Risk register**
- **B Assumption log**
- **C Updates to the risk report**
- **D Work performance reports**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer relates to updates to a project document that has summary conclusions about
risks.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is the process of prioritizing individual project risks for
further analysis or action by assessing their probability of occurrence and impact as well as other
characteristics. This process has one output, project documents updates, which contains four
documents that are updated:
● Assumption log
● Issue log
● Risk register
● Risk report

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register itself is not an output of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis
process, whereas updates to the risk register may be part of project document updates that
take place in this process. Besides, the risk register contains information on all identified
risks, but it does not contain a summary conclusion.
- **B Assumption log**
Incorrect. The assumption log provides information on assumptions and constraints but
does not provide a prioritized risk listing or a summary conclusion. Also, the assumption
log itself is not listed as an output of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process
although updates to the assumption log may be part of project document updates that take
place in this process.
- **C Updates to the risk report**
Correct. Updates to the risk report is an output of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis
that includes both a prioritized list of identified risks and a summary conclusion.
- **D Work performance reports**
Incorrect. Work performance reports are not an output of the Perform Qualitative Risk
Analysis process

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 419, 427

Question 41 of 210
Question ID: 651514
Which of the following is a tool and technique of the Plan Risk Management Process?
- **A Meetings**
- **B Representations of uncertainty**
- **C Change requests**
- **D Audits**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer absolutely must be used during a planning process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Plan Risk Management is the process of defining how to conduct risk management activities for
a project. This process has the following three tools & techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data analysis
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Meetings**
Correct. Meetings are used extensively during the Plan Risk Management process to collect
input, develop the plan, and obtain agreement from a variety of stakeholders.
- **B Representations of uncertainty**
Incorrect. Representations of uncertainty are not used in the Plan Risk Management
process but are instead employed during the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process.
- **C Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are formal proposal documents, not tools or techniques.
- **D Audits**
Incorrect. Risk audits are not an input of the Plan Risk Management process. They are a
tool and technique that may be incorporated into the risk management plan during this
process, for later implementation during the Monitor Risks process.

Question 42 of 210
Question ID: 651539
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Develop Project Charter process?
- **A Prototypes**
- **B Change control meetings**
- **C Expert judgment**
- **D Business case**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Technical knowledge of the industry could be helpful when developing a project charter.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Develop Project Charter process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Meetings
It is in this process where a document that formally authorizes the existence of a project is
developed. The charter provides the project manager with the authority to apply organizational
resources to project activities.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Prototypes**
Incorrect. Prototypes are listed as a tool and technique used in the Collect Requirements
process, not the Develop Project Charter process.
- **B Change control meetings**
Incorrect. Meetings, usually change control meetings, is a tool and technique used in the
Perform Integrated Change Control process, not the Develop Project Charter process.
- **C Expert judgment**
Correct. Expert judgment is a tool and technique used in the Develop Project Charter
process.
- **D Business case**
Incorrect. A business case is not a tool or technique. The business case is an example of a
business document that is commonly used as an input to the Develop Project Charter
process.

Question ID: 651699
Which of the below is not an input of the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process?
- **A Assumption log**
- **B Risk register**
- **C Stakeholder engagement plan**
- **D Communications management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer cannot be an input to the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Plan Stakeholder Engagement is the process of developing approaches to involve project
stakeholders, based on their needs, expectations, interests, and potential impact on the project.
This process has the following six inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan (including the communications management plan)
● Project documents (including the assumption log and the risk register)
● Agreements
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Assumption log**
Incorrect. The assumption log is an input to the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process that
contains information about assumptions and constraints that may be linked to specific
stakeholders.
- **B Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is an input to the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process that
links identified risks to specific stakeholders as either risk owners or as subject to risk
impact.
- **C Stakeholder engagement plan**
Correct. The stakeholder engagement plan is not an input but is instead the primary output
of the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **D Communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan is an input to the Plan Stakeholder
Engagement process that contains communications strategies for stakeholder engagement.

Question 45 of 210
Question ID: 651574
Which of the following is a tool and technique of the Develop Schedule process?
- **A Agile release planning**
- **B Expert judgment**
- **C Resource calendars**
- **D Analogous estimating**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Consider how the project development approach can affect the Develop Schedule process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Develop Schedule process has the following eight tools and techniques:
● Schedule network analysis
● Critical path method
● Resource optimization
● Data analysis
● Leads and lags
● Schedule compression
● Project management information system
● Agile release planning

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Agile release planning**
Correct. Agile release planning provides a high-level summary timeline of the release
schedule and determines the number of iterations or sprints in the release. Agile release
planning is a tool and technique that may be used in the Develop Schedule process.
- **B Expert judgment**
Incorrect. While expert judgment is a tool and technique used in numerous processes, it is
not listed in the PMBOK® Guide as a tool and technique used in the Develop Schedule
process. Therefore, expert judgment is not the best answer to the question asked.
- **C Resource calendars**
Incorrect. Resource calendars are an example of a project document. It is neither a tool or
technique.
- **D Analogous estimating**
Incorrect. Analogous estimating is a technique for estimating the duration or cost of an
activity using historical data from similar activities. Analogous estimating is used in the
Estimate Activity Durations process, which precedes the Develop Schedule process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 46 of 210
Question ID: 651523
Which of the following techniques may need to use duration estimates?
Top of Form
- **A Sensitivity analysis**
- **B Modeling and simulation**
- **C Probability and impact matrix**
- **D SWOT analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Duration estimates are often revised in quantitative risk analysis.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In modeling and simulation, the project model is iteratively computed with input values chosen
randomly from the cost or schedule estimates for each iteration and the probability distribution of
these variables. SWOT analysis is used during the Identify Risks process. Probability and impact
matrix is an example of a data representation technique used in the Perform Qualitative Risk
Analysis process. Sensitivity analysis is used to compare the relative impact of risks on project
objectives and also does not required to create duration estimates.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Sensitivity analysis**
Incorrect. Sensitivity analysis is a technique used to analyze the impact of each uncertainty
factor to the project objectives to determine which risks have the most impact on the
project. It is not necessary to use duration estimates in conducting sensitivity analysis.
- **B Modeling and simulation**
Correct. Modeling and simulation help to translate the uncertainties into the quantitative
impact on project objectives by calculating the probability distribution with the random
value chosen from the cost or schedule estimates.
- **C Probability and impact matrix**
Incorrect. Probability and impact matrix is applied to rank project risks based on their
probability of occurrence and impacts on project objectives.
- **D SWOT analysis**
Incorrect. SWOT analysis is a technique used to identify project risks by examining the
organization and project from the strengths, weaknesses, opportunities, and threats. This
technique does not need to use duration estimates.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 433
Bottom of Form

Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 47 of 210
Question ID: 651578
The Estimate Costs process has three outputs, including:
● Cost estimates
● Project documents updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
- **A Cost management plan**
- **B Resource requirements**
- **C Basis of estimates**
- **D Organizational process assets updates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Estimate Costs is the process of developing an approximation of the monetary resources needed
to complete project activities.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Estimate Costs is the process of developing an approximation of the monetary resources needed
to complete project work. It has the following three outputs:
● Cost estimates
● Basis of estimates
● Project document updates (assumption log, lessons learned register, and risk register)

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cost management plan**
Incorrect. The cost management plan is an input that describes estimating methods that can
be used and the level of precision and accuracy required for the cost estimate.
- **B Resource requirements**
Incorrect. Resource requirements is an input that identifies the types and quantities of
resources required for each work package or activity.
- **C Basis of estimates**
Correct. The basis of estimates documents how the estimates were established. The basis of
estimates is a critical output of the Estimate Costs process.
- **D Organizational process assets updates**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not identify any organizational process assets or
OPAs to update.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 240, 241, 242, and 247
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 48 of 210
Question ID: 651570
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Estimate Activity Durations process?
- **A Decomposition**
- **B Activity attributes**
- **C Parametric estimating**
- **D Facilitated workshops**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the purpose of the Estimate Activity Durations process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Estimate Activity Durations Process is where the number of work periods needed to
complete individual activities with the estimated resources are estimated. This process has the
following eight tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Analogous estimating
● Parametric estimating
● Three-point estimating
● Bottom-up estimating
● Data analysis
● Decision making
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Decomposition**
Incorrect. Decomposition is a technique used for dividing and subdividing the project scope
into smaller, more manageable parts. Decomposition is performed during the Define
Activities process, which precedes the Estimate Activity Durations process.
- **B Activity attributes**
Incorrect. Activity attributes are considered a project document and are inputs to the
Estimate Activity Durations process rather than a tool or technique.
- **C Parametric estimating**
Correct. Parametric estimating is an estimating technique used in the Estimate Activity
Durations process in which an algorithm is used to calculate duration based on historical
data and project parameters.
- **D Facilitated workshops**
Incorrect. Facilitated workshops are an example of the interpersonal and team skills tool
and technique and are not listed in the PMBOK® Guide as a tool and technique used in the
Estimate Activity Durations process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 195, 200
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 49 of 210
Question ID: 651644
The Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process has five tools and techniques, including:
● Data gathering
● Expert judgment
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Data analysis
Which of the following tools and techniques is missing from the list?
- **A Representations of uncertainty**
- **B Statistical sampling**
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
- **D Assumption and constraint analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis is the process of numerically analyzing the effect of
identified risks and other sources of uncertaintyon overall project objectives.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis is the process of numerically analyzing the effect of
identified individual project risks and other sources of uncertainty on overall project objectives.
This process has five tools and techniques, including:
● Data gathering

---

● Expert judgment
● Representations of uncertainty
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Data analysis

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Representations of uncertainty**
Correct. Representations of uncertainty is a technique employed during the Perform
Quantitative Risk Analysis process that enables a variety of different ways to represent
uncertainty for planned activities, including probability distributions (such as triangular,
normal, lognormal, beta, uniform, and discrete), as well as probabilistic branches.
- **B Statistical sampling**
Incorrect. Statistical sampling is a technique used during the Control Quality process to
choose a limited part of a population for inspection. It is not a tool or technique used in the
Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process.
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
Incorrect. Although cost-benefit analysis is a technique used during the Plan Risk
Responses process, it is not used during the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process.
- **D Assumption and constraint analysis**
Incorrect. Assumption and constraint analysis is a technique used during the Identify Risks
process to explore the validity of assumptions and constraints. It is not a tool or technique
used in the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 428, 432

Question ID: 651665
Which of the following processes uses expert judgment as a tool and technique?
- **A Validate Scope**
- **B Develop Schedule**
- **C Develop Team**
- **D Develop Project Management Plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Expert judgment is a commonly used tool and technique in the Planning Process Group.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Develop Project Management Plan is the process of defining, preparing, and coordinating all
plan components and consolidating them into an integrated project management plan. This
process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Validate Scope**
Incorrect. The Validate Scope process uses the tools and techniques of inspection and
decision making, but not expert judgment.
- **B Develop Schedule**
Incorrect. The Develop Schedule process uses eight tools and techniques, but expert
judgment is not one of them.
- **C Develop Team**
Incorrect. While the Develop Team process uses eight tools and techniques, expert
judgment is not among them.
- **D Develop Project Management Plan**
Correct. Expert judgment is one of the tools and techniques used in the Develop Project
Management Plan process.

Question 51 of 210
Question ID: 651529
What enterprise environmental factors can influence the Estimate Activity Resources process?
Top of Form
- **A Duration estimating databases**
- **B Staffing policies and procedures**
- **C Resource location, availability, and skill**
- **D Productivity metrics**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Consider what choice is actually an EEF that would help identify the type and quantities of
human resources, materials, equipment, and supplies necessary for members of your project
teams to complete project activities in the environment where they work.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Resource location, resource availability, and skills are all enterprise environmental factors that
can influence the Estimate Activity Resources process, along with organizational culture,
published estimating data, and marketplace conditions. These factors help to identify the type
and quantities of human resources, materials, equipment, and supplies necessary for members of
your project teams to complete project activities in the environment where they work.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Duration estimating databases**
Incorrect. Duration estimating databases are an EEF that influence the Estimate Activity
Durations process, but not the Estimate Activity Resources process.
- **B Staffing policies and procedures**
Incorrect. Staffing policies and procedures are not enterprise environmental factors, but
organizational process assets.
- **C Resource location, availability, and skill**
Correct. Resource location is an EEF that serves as an input to both the Estimate Activity
Durations and Estimate Activity Resources processes, and resource availability is an EEF
that serves as an input to Estimate Activity Durations process.
- **D Productivity metrics**
Incorrect. Productivity metrics are an EEF that influence the Estimate Activity Durations
process, but not the Estimate Activity Resources process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 323

Question 52 of 210
Question ID: 651593
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Manage Quality process?
- **A Quality metrics**
- **B Problem solving**
- **C Reserve analysis**
- **D Meetings**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Manage Quality process is concerned with product design and process improvements.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Manage Quality process has the following eight tools and techniques:
● Data gathering
● Data analysis
● Decision making
● Data representation
● Audits
● Design for X
● Problem solving
● Quality improvement methods

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Quality metrics**
Incorrect. Quality metrics are inputs to the Manage Quality process. They are not classified
as a tool or technique.
- **B Problem solving**
Correct. Effective and systematic problem solving is a fundamental element in quality
assurance and quality improvement. Therefore, problem solving is a tool and technique
used in the Manage Quality process.
- **C Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis is a technique used to determine the amount of contingency and
management reserves needed for the project. The PMBOK® Guide does not include reserve
analysis among the tools and techniques used in the Manage Quality process.
- **D Meetings**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not include meetings among the tools and techniques
used in the Manage Quality process.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 53 of 210
Question ID: 651604
Which of the following is not a tool or technique of the Develop Team process?
- **A Team-building activities**
- **B Virtual teams**
- **C Training**
- **D Resource optimization**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Develop Team is the process of improving the competencies, team interaction, and the overall
team environment.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Develop Team is the process of improving competences, team member interaction, and overall
team environment to enhance project performance. It has the following eight tools and
techniques:
● Colocation
● Virtual teams
● Communication technology (shared portal, video conferencing, audio conferencing,
email/chat)
● Interpersonal and team skills (conflict management, influencing, motivation, negotiation,
team building)
● Recognition and rewards
● Training (competencies)

---

● Individual and team assessments (preferences, aspirations, information processing,
decision making, work relationships)
● Meetings (project orientation, team building, team development)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Team-building activities**
Incorrect. Team building activities, along with project orientation and team development,
are among the meetings that serve as a tool for the Develop Team process. In addition,
team building serves as an interpersonal and team skill that can be used for this process.
- **B Virtual teams**
Incorrect. Using technology to create an online team environment where the team can share
digital resources and use conversation threads to discuss issues is a valid tool for the
Develop Project Team process for improving interaction among remote team members.
- **C Training**
Incorrect. Training is a tool designed to enhance the competencies of the project team
members and is used to develop the team.
- **D Resource optimization**
Correct. Resource optimization is a tool of the Develop Schedule and Control Schedule
processes, not the Develop Team process.

**Reference:**

em> – Sixth Edition, Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 340-342

Question 54 of 210
Question ID: 651546
Which of the following is an input to the Perform Integrated Change Control process?
- **A Agreements**
- **B Work performance reports**
- **C Change request status updates**
- **D Change log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What type of information would be required to decide as to whether to approve change requests?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Perform Integrated Change Control process has the following six inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Work performance reports
● Change requests
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
Perform Integrated Change Control is the process of reviewing all change requests; approving
changes and managing changes to deliverables, organizational process assets, project documents,
and the project management plan; and communicating the decisions.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Agreements**
Incorrect. Agreements are not inputs to the Perform Integrated Change Control process.
- **B Work performance reports**
Correct. Work performance reports are inputs to the Perform Integrated Change Control
process. Reports of interest to the process include resource availability, schedule and cost
data, and earned value reports.
- **C Change request status updates**
Incorrect. 'Change request status updates' is not a term used in the PMBOK® Guide.
- **D Change log**
Incorrect. The change log is an output, not an input of the Perform Integrated Change
Control process.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 55 of 210
Question ID: 651599
Which of the following is not an input to the Plan Resource Management process?
- **A Work performance information**
- **B Organizational process assets**
- **C Requirements documentation**
- **D Enterprise environmental factors**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Plan Resource Management belongs to the Planning Process Group, and the resource
management plan should be created before execution begins.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Plan Resource Management process has the following five inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan (quality management plan and scope baseline)
● Project documents (project schedule, requirements documentation, risk register,
stakeholder register)
● Enterprise environmental factors or EEFs (culture, structure, geographic distribution,
existing team’s competencies and availability, and market conditions)
● Organizational process assets or OPAs (policies and procedures for human resources,
physical resource management, safety, security, templates for the resource management
plan, and historical project information)

---

Work performance information is not an input to the Plan Resource Management process. Work
performance data is an output of the Executing process, Direct and Manage Project Work.
Control Resources is one of the Monitoring and Controlling processes that analyze the data to
output work performance information. In turn, this information serves as an input to Monitor and
Control Project Work so that data analysis can produce work performance reports. These reports
feed into the Perform Integrated Change Control, Manage Team, Manage Communications, and
Monitor Risks processes.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance information**
Correct. Work performance information is generated during the Monitoring and
Controlling Process Group but only after the processes in the Executing Process Group
generate work performance data. In turn, work performance information serves as input to
four processes, including Manage Team, not Plan Resource Management processes.
- **B Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Organizational process assets or OPAs influence the guidance included in the
resource management plan. OPAs are inputs to the Plan Resource Management process.
- **C Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation is a project document that serves as an input to the
Plan Resource Management process. The type and amount of resources needed may dictate
how the resources should be managed.
- **D Enterprise environmental factors**
Incorrect. Enterprise environmental factors or EEFs also influence the guidance provided
in the resource management plan. EEFs are inputs to the Plan Resource Management
process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 314
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

Question 56 of 210
Question ID: 651507
Which of the following components of the project management plan is an input to the Plan Risk
Management process?
Top of Form
- **A Scope management plan**
- **B Schedule management plan**
- **C Communications management plan**
- **D All components of the project management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is there a subsidiary plan of the project management plan that has zero influence on the Risk
Management Plan?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In planning risk management, all approved subsidiary management plans should be taken into
consideration to make the risk management plan consistent with them. The methodologies
outlined in the various project management plan components might influence the Plan Risk
Management process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Scope management plan**
Incorrect. The scope management plan is an input to the Plan Risk Management process.
Scope definition and change are important sources of risk for projects. However, this choice
is not the best option for the question asked.
- **B Schedule management plan**
Incorrect. The schedule management plan is an input to the Plan Risk Management
process. The timing of various risk management activities must be coordinated with the rest
of the project schedule. However, this choice is not the best option for the question asked.
- **C Communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan is an input to the Plan Risk Management
process. The communication of risks and risk responses needs to be coordinated and
integrated with the other project communications activities. However, this choice is not the
best option for the question asked.
- **D All components of the project management plan**
Correct. This statement is true. Information in the various project management plan
components might influence the Plan Risk Management process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 402-403

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 57 of 210
Question ID: 651625
The Manage Communications process has five inputs, including:
● Project documents
● Work performance reports
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
Which of the following inputs is missing from the list?
- **A Change log**
- **B Issue log**
- **C Resource management plan**
- **D Lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the answers are considered project documents?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Manage Communications is the process of ensuring timely and appropriate collection, creation,
distribution, storage, retrieval, management, monitoring, and the ultimate disposition of project
information. This process has the following five inputs:
● Project management plan (e.g., resource management plan)
● Project documents

---

● Work performance reports
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change log**
Incorrect. The change log is used to communicate changes and approved, rejected, and
deferred change requests to the impacted stakeholders. The change log is an example of
project documents, which are inputs to the Manage Communications process. Project
documents are already listed in the question.
- **B Issue log**
Incorrect. The issue log is used to communicate information about issues to stakeholders.
The issue log is an example of project documents, which are inputs to the Manage
Communications process. Project documents are on the list in the question.
- **C Resource management plan**
Correct. The resource management plan describes the communications that are needed for
management of the team or physical resources. The resource management plan is a
component of the project management plan which is an input to the Manage
Communications process. The project management plan is missing from the list in the
question.
- **D Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. Lessons learned earlier in the project concerning communications can be
applied later in the project to improve the communication process. The lessons learned
register is an example of project documents which are inputs to the Manage
Communications process. Project documents are on the list in the question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 379, 381

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 58 of 210
Question ID: 651515
Which element of the project management plan is not typically updated as an output of the
Conduct Procurements process?
- **A Communications management plan**
- **B Change management plan**
- **C Scope baseline**
- **D Procurement management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Would the Conduct Procurements process affect the organization's formal change control policy?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Conduct Procurements is the process of obtaining seller responses, selecting a seller, and
awarding a contract. This process has the following six outputs:
● Selected sellers
● Agreements
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (e.g., communications management plan, scope
baseline, procurement management plan)
● Project documents updates
● Organizational process assets

---

While change requests can be submitted as a result of carrying out the Conduct Procurements
process, the change management plan itself is not typically updated during that process. All the
other choices represent elements of the project management plan that may be updated during the
Conduct Procurements process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communications management plan**
Incorrect. As sellers are hired, the communications management plan is updated to
incorporate their communications needs and approaches.
- **B Change management plan**
Correct. The change management plan describes how the change control system will be
implemented. The Conduct Procurements process is not likely to have any impact on this
plan. Therefore, the change management plan is the correct answer.
- **C Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The project WBS and deliverables documented in the scope baseline may change
during the procurement process.
- **D Procurement management plan**
Incorrect. The contracting and negotiating processes used during procurement may result
in an update to the procurement management plan.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 482, 490

Question 59 of 210
Question ID: 651577
The Control Schedule process has five outputs, including:
● Schedule forecasts
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
- **A Work performance reports**
- **B Work performance information**
- **C Organizational process assets updates (OPAs)**
- **D Budget forecasts**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is a common output from the controlling processes.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Control Schedule process has the following five outputs:
● Work performance information
● Schedule forecasts
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates

---

● Project documents updates
This process is defined as "the process of monitoring the status of the project to update the
project schedule and manage changes to the schedule baseline".

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance reports**
Incorrect. Work performance information produced by the controlling processes is
combined into a physical or electronic representation and distributed as work performance
reports. Work performance reports are outputs of the Monitor and Control Project Work
process, not the Control Schedule process.
- **B Work performance information**
Correct. Work performance information is an output from the Control Schedule process and
includes information on how project work is performing compared to the schedule baseline.
Work performance information is the output missing from the question, and, therefore, the
correct answer.
- **C Organizational process assets updates (OPAs)**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not list OPAs updates as outputs of the Control
Schedule process.
- **D Budget forecasts**
Incorrect. Schedule forecasts, not budget forecasts, are outputs from the Control Schedule
process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 223, 228

Question ID: 651544
Which of the following is an output of the Monitor and Control Project Work process?
- **A Milestone list**
- **B Enterprise environmental factors updates**
- **C Organizational process assets updates**
- **D Project documents updates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Forecasts are likely to change as a result of the Monitor and Control Project Work process.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Monitor and Control Project Work process has the following four outputs:
● Work performance reports
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
Monitor and Control Project Work is the process of tracking, reviewing, and reporting overall
progress to meet the performance objectives defined in the project management plan.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Milestone list**
Incorrect. The milestone list shows the scheduled dates for specific milestones and is used
to check if the planned milestones have been met. The milestone list is an input to the
Monitor and Control Project Work process, not an output.
- **B Enterprise environmental factors updates**
Incorrect. Enterprise environmental factors are only updated as a result of the executing
processes in Project Resource Management.
- **C Organizational process assets updates**

Control Project Work process.
- **D Project documents updates**
Correct. Cost forecasts, issue log, lessons learned register, risk register, and schedule
forecasts are all examples of project documents that may be updated as a result of the
Monitor and Control Project Work process.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 61 of 210
Question ID: 651561
The Define Activities process has four tools and techniques, including:
● Decomposition
● Expert judgment
● Meetings
Which of the following tools and techniques is missing from the list?
- **A Rolling wave planning**
- **B Alternative analysis**
- **C Audits**
- **D Project management information system**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Define Activities is the process of identifying the specific actions to be performed to produce the
project deliverables but sometimes a project cannot be planned completely.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Define Activities process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Decomposition
● Rolling wave planning

---

● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Rolling wave planning**
Correct. Rolling wave planning is an iterative planning technique in which work to be
accomplished in the near term is planned in detail, while work further in the future is
planned at a higher level. Rolling wave planning is a tool and technique used in the Define
Activities process.
- **B Alternative analysis**
Incorrect. Alternative analysis is a data analysis tool and technique used to evaluate
options to select the best approach for accomplishing project work. Alternative analysis is
not a tool or technique listed in the PMBOK® Guide for the Define Activities process.
- **C Audits**
Incorrect. An audit is a structured review of a process. An audit may reveal if a process is
complying with organizational policies or if contracts are accurate and complete. Audits
are not a tool or technique listed in the PMBOK® Guide for the Define Activities process.
- **D Project management information system**
Incorrect. A project management information system (PMIS) consists of the tools and
techniques used to gather, integrate, and disseminate the outputs of project management
processes. A PMIS is not a tool or technique listed in the PMBOK® Guide for the Define
Activities process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 183, 185

Question 63 of 210
Question ID: 651537
Which of the following processes assesses the quality of risk data?
Top of Form
- **A Identify Risks**
- **B Plan Risk Responses**
- **C Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis**
- **D Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Risk data should be assessed before performing risk analysis.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Risk data quality assessment is part of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process to evaluate
risk data in terms of the accuracy, reliability, and integrity. It is very important because
low-quality risk data may lead to poor qualitative risk analysis and subsequent response
planning. An evaluation of the quality of the risk data also helps to clarify the assessment of each
risk's importance to the project.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Identify Risks**
Incorrect. The Identify Risks process focuses on identifying potential project threats and
opportunities but does not assess risk data quality.
- **B Plan Risk Responses**
Incorrect. The Plan Risk Response process determines how risk management (and all the
other risk-related processes) will be conducted, but it does not assess the quality of risk
data.
- **C Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis**
Correct. The Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process includes assessing the quality of
risk data to ensure it is reliable and good for use.
- **D Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis**
Incorrect. Quantitative risk analysis is focused on the numerical analysis of the combined
effect of risks, and not on the quality of risk data.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 423, 420
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 64 of 210
Question ID: 651560
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Control Scope process?
Top of Form
- **A Work performance information**
- **B Audits**
- **C Inspection**
- **D Variance analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Control Scope is the process of monitoring the status of the project and product scope and
managing changes to the Scope Baseline.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Control Scope process is where the status of the project is monitored. It is also where the
product scope and changes to the scope baseline are managed. The process has only one tool and
technique, data analysis, which includes variance analysis and trend analysis.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Work performance information**
Incorrect. Work performance information is not a tool or technique but is instead an input
of Monitor and Control Project Work process and output of many processes under the
Monitoring and Controlling Process Group including the Control Scope process.
- **B Audits**
Incorrect. For effectively executing quality activities and identifying causes of poor quality,
audits are tools of the Manage Quality process, not the Control Scope process.
- **C Inspection**
Incorrect. Inspection is a tool and technique for Validate Scope and other Monitoring and
Controlling processes, but not for the Control Scope process, which is concerned with
monitoring the status of the project and product scope and managing changes to the scope
baseline, which involves analysis of work performance data instead of involving inspection
of deliverables.
- **D Variance analysis**
Correct. Variance analysis is a data analysis tool used in the Control Scope process to
compare the baseline to the actual results and determine if the variance is within the
threshold amount or if corrective or preventive action is appropriate.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 170
Bottom of Form

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 65 of 210
Question ID: 651541
Which of the following is not an input to the Develop Project Management Plan process?
- **A Project charter**
- **B Organizational process assets**
- **C Work performance reports**
- **D Outputs from other processes**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Develop Project Management Plan process is in the Planning Process Group.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Develop Project Management Plan process has the following four inputs:
● Project charter
● Outputs from other processes
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
It is in this process where all plan components are defined, prepared, coordinated, and
consolidated into an integrated project management plan.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter**
Incorrect. The project team uses the project charter as a starting point for initial project
planning. Therefore, the project charter is an input to the Develop Project Management
Plan process.
- **B Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Historical information, lessons learned repository, and project management plan
templates are examples of organizational process assets that may be used as inputs to the
Develop Project Management Plan process.
- **C Work performance reports**
Correct. Work performance reports are inputs to the Perform Integrated Change Control
process but not the Develop Project Management Plan process. Therefore, 'work
performance reports' is the correct answer to the question asked.
- **D Outputs from other processes**
Incorrect. Outputs from other processes are integrated to create the project management
plan. Subsidiary plans and baselines that are outputs from other planning processes are
inputs to the Develop Project Management Plan process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 82

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 66 of 210
Question ID: 651505
Which of the following is not a tool or technique used in the Define Activities process?
- **A Bottom-up estimating**
- **B Decomposition**
- **C Rolling wave planning**
- **D Expert judgment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is a tool or technique used after the Define Activities process is complete.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Define Activities process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Decomposition
● Rolling wave planning
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Bottom-up estimating**
Correct. Bottom-up estimating is used to estimate activity costs and the resources required
to execute an activity, which happens 'after' activities are defined.
- **B Decomposition**
Incorrect. Decomposition is a technique used in the Define Activities process to divide or
subdivide the project scope and project deliverables into smaller more manageable parts.
- **C Rolling wave planning**
Incorrect. Rolling wave planning is a technique used in the Define Activities process where
the work to be accomplished in the near-term is planned in detail, while the work in the
future is planned at a higher level.
- **D Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is a technique used in the Define Activities process where
project team members or other experts, who are experienced and skilled in developing
detailed project scope statements, the WBS, and project schedules, can provide expertise in
defining activities.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 183

Question 67 of 210
Question ID: 651619
The Manage Stakeholder Engagement process has three outputs, including:
● Change requests
● Project documents updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
- **A Project management plan updates**
- **B Work performance information**
- **C Meetings**
- **D Milestone list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What major artifacts from this process help guide it and will typically be updated during
execution?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the process of communicating and working with
stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations, address issues, and foster appropriate
stakeholder involvement. The Manage Stakeholder Engagement process has three outputs,
including:
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (e.g., the communications plan, the stakeholder
engagement plan)

---

● Project document updates (including the change log, the issue log, the lessons learned
register, and the stakeholder register)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project management plan updates**
Correct. Two components of the project management plan are updated during the Manage
Stakeholder engagement process: the communications management plan and the
stakeholder engagement plan.
- **B Work performance information**
Incorrect. Work performance information is not an output of the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process.
- **C Meetings**
Incorrect. Although this process may involve a variety of meetings, a meeting is a
technique, not an output.
- **D Milestone list**
Incorrect. Milestone lists are outputs of the Define Activities process. Milestone lists are not
outputs of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 523

Question 68 of 210
Question ID: 651690
One of the project management processes results in only one output. This output specifies the
level of precision.
What output is that?
Top of Form
- **A Stakeholder engagement plan**
- **B Schedule management plan**
- **C Project management plan**
- **D Cost management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of the process in which stakeholders want to see the most precision.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Level of precision is defined in the cost management plan. An important distinction should be
noted. The 'level of precision' is the degree to which cost estimates will be rounded up or down
(e.g., $9,995.59 to $10,000), based on the scope of the activities and magnitude of the project.
The 'level of accuracy' is the acceptable range (e.g., 10%) used in determining realistic cost
estimates is specified and may include an amount for contingencies.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Stakeholder engagement plan**
Incorrect. The Plan Stakeholder Engagement process only has one output, which is the
stakeholder engagement plan. However, this plan does not include the level of precision.
- **B Schedule management plan**
Incorrect. The Plan Schedule Management process only has one output, which is the
schedule management plan. The schedule management plan only has one output but does
not include the level of precision.
- **C Project management plan**
Incorrect. The Develop Project Management Plan process has only one output, but the
project management plan does not include the level of precision.
- **D Cost management plan**
Correct. The cost management plan includes the level of precision along with other key
attributes, such as level of accuracy, units of measure, and control thresholds. The cost
management plan is the sole output of the Plan Cost Management process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 238
Bottom of Form

Top of Form
Question 69 of 210
Question ID: 651661
If change requests can occur throughout a project but must be approved by the change control
board, all of the following are true except?
Top of Form
- **A Change requests are outputs of many processes of the Executing Process Group and Monitoring**
and Controlling Process Group.
- **B New change requests are inputs to the Perform Integrated Change Control process, while**
approved change requests are its outputs.
- **C New change requests are inputs to the Direct and Manage Project Work, while approved change**
requests are outputs of this process.
- **D Approved change requests are inputs to three processes: Direct and Manage Project Work,**
Control Quality, and Control Procurements.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

There is only one process, where approved change requests are outputs and only three processes
where those approved change requests are inputs. Remember, you are looking for the false
statement that is the exception.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Many processes produce change requests as outputs, but only the Perform Integrated Change
Control process has change requests as inputs. Likewise, only the Perform Integrated Change
Control process has approved change requests as outputs. Approved change requests are inputs

---

to the Direct and Manage Project Work, Control Quality, and Control Procurements processes.
During the Direct and Manage Project Work process, approved changes are implemented, and
during the Control Quality and Control Procurements processes, implementation of the approved
changes is verified.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change requests are outputs of many processes of the Executing Process Group and**
Monitoring and Controlling Process Group.
Incorrect. This statement is true. Carrying out processes that belong to the Executing
Process Group and Monitoring and Controlling Process Group may result in change
requests.
- **B New change requests are inputs to the Perform Integrated Change Control process, while**
approved change requests are its outputs.
Incorrect. This statement is true. Perform Integrated Change Control is the only process
where approved change requests are outputs. During this process, the change control board
considers whether to approve change requests from other processes.
- **C New change requests are inputs to the Direct and Manage Project Work, while approved**
change requests are outputs of this process.
Correct. This statement is false. New change requests are not inputs to the Direct and
Manage Project Work but are outputs. Perform Integrated Change Control is the only
process where approved change requests are outputs.
- **D Approved change requests are inputs to three processes: Direct and Manage Project Work,**
Control Quality, and Control Procurements.
Incorrect. This statement is true. Approved change requests come to these processes from
the Perform Integrated Change Control process for implementation and verification that
the changes have been implemented.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 93, 301, 496
Bottom of Form

Question 70 of 210
Question ID: 651566
Which of the following is an input to the Estimate Activity Durations process?
- **A Resource calendars**
- **B Basis of estimates**
- **C Requirements documentation**
- **D Verified deliverables**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Estimate Activity Durations is the process of estimating the number of work periods needed to
complete individual activities with estimated resources.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Estimate Activity Durations process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., resource calendars)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Resource calendars**
Correct. Resource calendars specify when and how long identified project resources will be
available during the project. Resource calendars are an example of the project documents
that are inputs to the Estimate Activity Durations process.
- **B Basis of estimates**
Incorrect. The basis of estimates is supporting documentation providing a clear
understanding of how the duration estimate was derived. The basis of estimates is an output
(not an input) of the Estimate Activity Durations process.
- **C Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation describes how individual requirements meet the
business need for the project and is an output from the Collect Requirements process, not
an input to the Estimate Activity Durations process.
- **D Verified deliverables**
Incorrect. Verified deliverables are deliverables that have been checked for correctness
during the Control Quality process. Verified deliverables are inputs of the Validate Scope
process, not the Estimate Activity Durations process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 195, 199

Question 71 of 210
Question ID: 651372
The project has reached a stage where work is being done in seven countries. Project team
members need to know in which currency they are to report their cost data.
Which of the following should they reference?
Top of Form
- **A Cost baseline**
- **B Cost management plan**
- **C Cost estimates**
- **D Cost breakdown structure**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where would one find guidance on how to manage cost-related project processes?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The cost management plan provides information and guidance on how the project manager and
project team are to plan, structure, account, and control the project costs. The contents of the plan
vary based on the needs of the particular project. The project in the scenario is operating in many
countries and currencies. To align all the project documents and communications, it is important
for this project's cost management plan to detail the currencies to use or not use, when, in which
circumstances, and other pertinent requirements of the project. The plan is the go-to location for
the team to use the proper cost denotations.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cost baseline**
Incorrect. The cost baseline is used as a comparison to gauge the progress and status of the
project cost management. The cost baseline does not list the policies on currency
denotations.
- **B Cost management plan**
Correct. The cost management plan contains information and guidance on how to best
manage the cost elements and processes of the project. This includes information on the
currencies and other symbols to use for reports, records, calculations, and other project
management needs.
- **C Cost estimates**
Incorrect. Cost estimates are quantitative assessments of the probable costs required to
complete project work. Cost estimates do not provide guidance of the currency to be used
on the project. It is the cost management plan that specifies the currency in which costs are
estimated during project planning and reported during execution and monitoring and
controlling.
- **D Cost breakdown structure**
Incorrect. 'Cost breakdown structure' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 238-239

Question 72 of 210
Question ID: 626024
Which of the following is often required by the buyer and should be supported by the seller to
verify compliance of the seller's work processes and deliverables?
Top of Form
- **A Performance reporting**
- **B Payment systems**
- **C Inspections and audits**
- **D Seller compliance evaluations**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What are the logical activities to verify compliance?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Inspections and audits are tools and techniques of the Control Procurements process, which are
used to verify compliance and the seller's work processes or deliverables. An inspection is a
structured review of the work being performed by the seller. This may involve a simple review of
the deliverables or an actual physical review of the work itself. Audits are a structured review of
the procurement process. Rights and obligations related to audits should be described in the
procurement contract.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Performance reporting**
Incorrect. Performance reporting provides management with information about how
effectively the seller is achieving the contractual objectives. Performance reporting is not a

---

means to verify the compliance of the seller's work processes or deliverables but rather a
measure of the seller's overall performance to date.
- **B Payment systems**
Incorrect. Payment systems are used to process payments to the seller after certification of
satisfactory work by an authorized person on the project team. Payment systems are not a
means to verify compliance of the seller's work processes and deliverables.
- **C Inspections and audits**
Correct. Inspections and audits are tools and techniques of Control Procurements process
used to verify compliance and the seller's work processes or deliverables.
- **D Seller compliance evaluations**
Incorrect. 'Seller compliance evaluations' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 498

Question 73 of 210
Question ID: 651618
Which of the following is an output of the Monitor Communications process?

---

Top of Form
- **A Organizational process assets updates (OPAs)**
- **B Work performance information**
- **C Team performance assessments**
- **D Work performance reports**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer is an output of many of the processes in the Monitoring and Controlling Process
Group?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Monitor Communications is the process of ensuring that the information needs of the project and
its stakeholders are met. It has the following four outputs:
● Work performance information
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Organizational process assets updates (OPAs)**
Incorrect. While OPAs updates are outputs to many project management processes, the
PMBOK® Guide does not include OPAs updates as an output from the Monitor
Communications process.
- **B Work performance information**
Correct. As with many of the processes in the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group,
work performance information are outputs of the Monitor Communications process.

---

- **C Team performance assessments**
Incorrect. Team performance assessments are outputs of the Develop Team process, not the
Monitor Communications process.
- **D Work performance reports**
Incorrect. Work performance reports are outputs of the Monitor and Control Project Work
process and an input to the Manage Communications process. However, work performance
reports are not an output of the Monitor Communications process.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Top of Form
Question 74 of 210
Question ID: 651557
Which of the following is not an input to the Validate Scope process?
Top of Form
- **A Requirements documentation**
- **B Business case**

---

- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
- **D Requirements management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Validate Scope is the process of formalizing acceptance of the completed project deliverables.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Validate Scope process is where the completed project deliverables are formally accepted.
The process has the following five inputs:
● the project management plan (especially the scope management plan, requirements
management plan, and scope baseline),
● project documents (especially the lessons learned register, quality reports, requirements
documentation, and requirements traceability matrix),
● verified deliverables (from the Control Quality process), and
● work performance data from the Direct and Manage Project Work process (including the degree
of compliance with requirements, number of nonconformities, the severity of the
nonconformities, or the number of validation cycles performed in a period).
In contrast, a business case is a phase gate document including an economic feasibility study,
business needs and requirements, basic scope, project objectives, and benefits, normally used in
Initiating a project. Therefore, a business case serves as an input business document for the
Develop Project Charter, Close Project or Phase, Collect Requirements, Determine Budget, Plan
Procurement Management and Identify Stakeholders processes, but not in the Validate Scope
process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. The requirements documentation is one of the project documents that serve as an
input to the Validate Scope process.
- **B Business case**

---

Correct. A business case is a phase gate document including an economic feasibility study,
business needs and requirements, and basic scope, which often serves as the basis for
authorizing the initiation of the project, not the Validate Scope process.
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is also one of the project documents that
serve as an input to the Validate Scope process.
- **D Requirements management plan**
Incorrect. The requirements management plan is a component of the project management
plan that serves as an input to the Validate Scope process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 165
Bottom of Form

Question 75 of 210
Question ID: 651629
The Monitor Risks process has four inputs, including:
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Work performance reports

---

Which of the following inputs is missing from the list?
Top of Form
- **A Work performance data**
- **B Change requests**
- **C Reserve analysis**
- **D Risk acceptance**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is an input to all the processes in the Monitoring and Controlling Process
Group.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Monitor Risks process has four inputs, including:
● Project management plan (e.g., the risk management plan)
● Project documents (including the issue log, the lessons learned register, the risk register, and the
risk report)
● Work performance data
● Work performance reports

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance data**
Correct. Work performance data is an input to the Monitor Risks process, where it provides
data on project status such as risk responses that have been implemented, risks that have
occurred, risks that are active, and those that have been closed out.
- **B Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are an output of rather than an input to the Monitor Risks
process.

---

- **C Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis is a tool and technique used during the Monitor Risks process,
not an input.
- **D Risk acceptance**
Incorrect. Risk acceptance is not an input but is instead a risk response strategy where a
specific risk is acknowledged, but no action is taken unless the risk occurs.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 453, 455

Which of the following is an output from the Develop Project Management Plan process?

to the Develop Project Management Plan process.
- **C Project documents updates**

Question 77 of 210
Question ID: 626023
The project manager in charge of the construction of a manufacturing plant in Asia is concerned
about the communications flow in the project because there are stakeholders from different
countries and cultures.
Which of the following should she use to be more efficient at facilitating discussions with timely
data?
Top of Form
- **A Work performance reports**
- **B Historical information**
- **C Communications performance reporting**
- **D Stakeholder register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the following is an input to the Manage Communications process?
Correct Answer: A

---


**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests the project manager is performing the Manage Communications process.
Work performance reports are an input to this process. Work performance reports are a collection
of project performance and status information that may be used to facilitate discussion and create
communications. Reports that are comprehensive, accurate, and available promptly may help the
project manager in facilitating discussions with timely data as asked by the question, making
work performance reports the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance reports**
Correct. Work performance reports are a collection of project performance and status
information that may be used to facilitate discussion and to create communications.
- **B Historical information**
Incorrect. Historical information consists of documents and data on prior projects
including project files, records, correspondence, closed contracts, and closed projects. The
question is asking for an item that would help in facilitating discussions with timely data
rather than historical data.
- **C Communications performance reporting**
Incorrect. 'Communications performance reporting' is not a concept specified in the
PMBOK® Guide.
- **D Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document that includes the identification,
assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. While this document may help the
project manager get better prepared for the discussions with various stakeholders, the
keyword in the question is timely data. The stakeholder register is not helpful in facilitating
discussions requiring timely data.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 382

Question 78 of 210
Question ID: 613676
You are looking for information on personnel rates, travel costs, and other costs that are needed
to estimate the overall project budget.
Where is the best place to find this information?
Top of Form
- **A Work breakdown structure (WBS)**
- **B Resource calendars**
- **C Resource management plan**
- **D Cost baseline**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What input to the Determine Budget process provides information on costs related to estimating
the project budget?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests you are carrying out the Determine Budget process. The resource
management plan is one of the inputs into that process. The resource management plan provides
information on rates (personnel and other resources), estimation of travel costs, and other

---

foreseen costs that are necessary to estimate the overall project budget. Therefore, the resource
management plan is the best place to find information on costs related to estimating the project
budget.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work breakdown structure (WBS)**
Incorrect. The work breakdown structure (WBS) is a hierarchical decomposition of the total
scope of work to be carried out by the project team. While the WBS (part of the scope
baseline) is among the inputs to the Determine Budget process described in the scenario,
the WBS does not have information on information on personnel rates or travel costs.
- **B Resource calendars**
Incorrect. A resource calendar identifies the working days and shifts upon which each
specific resource is available. A resource calendar does not provide information on costs.
- **C Resource management plan**
Correct. The resource management plan provides information on rates (personnel and
other resources), estimation of travel costs, and other foreseen costs that are necessary to
estimate the overall project budget.
- **D Cost baseline**
Incorrect. The question implies that the Determine Budget process is being carried out. The
cost baseline is an output of the Determine Budget process rather than its input.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 250
Bottom of Form

Question 79 of 210
Question ID: 651660
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Control Procurements process?
Top of Form
- **A Product analysis**
- **B Advertising**
- **C Earned value analysis**
- **D Market research**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Contract performance needs to be monitored to ensure the vendor is in compliance.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Control Procurements. The process of managing procurement relationships, monitoring contract
performance, making changes and corrections as appropriate, and closing contracts. It has the
following five tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Claims administration
● Data analysis (e.g., earned value analysis)
● Inspections
● Audits

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Product analysis**
Incorrect. Product analysis is a tool used to define the scope of projects that have a product
as a deliverable. Therefore, product analysis is not a tool or technique used in the Control
Procurements process.
- **B Advertising**
Incorrect. Advertising is a tool and technique used in the Conduct Procurements process,
not the Control Procurements process.
- **C Earned value analysis**
Correct. Earned value analysis is an example of a data analysis tool and technique used in
the Control Procurements process to calculate schedule and cost variances.
- **D Market research**
Incorrect. Market research is an example of a data gathering technique that is typically
used in the Plan Procurement Management process. The PMBOK® Guide does not include
market research in the tools and techniques used in the Control Procurements process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 492, 498

Question ID: 651501
Which of the processes below do not use meetings as a tool or technique?
Top of Form
- **A Define Scope**
- **B Plan Stakeholder Engagement**
- **C Monitor Risks**
- **D Identify Stakeholders**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think about the type of activities involved in each process and reflect on what purpose a meeting
would have for these activities.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Meetings are used as a tool and technique in many project management processes. However, as
far as the Project Scope Management Knowledge Area is concerned, meetings are only used in
the Plan Scope Management process. None of the other five processes of this Knowledge Area,
including the Define Scope process, uses meetings as their tools or techniques.

**Details for Each Option:**

Correct. Meetings are not among the tools and techniques explicitly listed for the Define
Scope process.
- **B Plan Stakeholder Engagement**

---

Incorrect. The Plan Stakeholder Engagement process uses meetings as a technique.
- **C Monitor Risks**
Incorrect. The Monitor Risks process uses meetings as a technique.
- **D Identify Stakeholders**
Incorrect. The Identify Stakeholders process uses meetings as a technique.
