Question 81 of 210
Question ID: 651542
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Direct and Manage Project Work process?
Top of Form
- **A Project management information system (PMIS)**
- **B Focus groups**

---

- **C Approved change requests**
- **D Product analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Consider what might be useful to gather and disseminate all the information that is required by a
project.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Direct and Manage Project Work is defined as the process of leading and performing the
work defined in the project management plan and implementing approved changes to achieve the
project's objectives. This process has the following three tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Project management information system
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project management information system (PMIS)**
Correct. A project management information system consists of the tools and techniques
used to gather, integrate, and disseminate the outputs of project management processes. A
PMIS is a tool and technique used in the Direct and Manage Project Work process.
- **B Focus groups**
Incorrect. Focus groups are an elicitation technique that brings together prequalified
stakeholders and subject matter experts to learn about their expectations and attitudes
about a proposed product, service, or result. Focus groups are listed as one of the types of
tools and techniques used in the Develop Project Charter and Develop Project
Management Plan processes but not the Direct and Manage Project Work process.
- **C Approved change requests**
Incorrect. Approved change requests are not classified as tools or techniques but are inputs
to the Direct and Manage Project Work process.

---

- **D Product analysis**
Incorrect. Product analysis is a tool to define scope and is, therefore, a tool and technique
used in the Define Scope process, but not in the Direct and Manage Project Work process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 90, 95

Question ID: 651587
Which of the following is an output of the Control Costs process?
Top of Form

- **B Activity duration estimates**
- **C Cost performance baseline**
- **D Cost forecasts**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

The Control Costs process enables monitoring the status of the project to update the project
budget and managing changes to the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Control Costs is the process of monitoring the status of the project to update the project costs and
manage changes to the cost baseline. The Control Costs process has the following outputs:
● Work performance information
● Cost forecasts
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project funding requirements**
Incorrect. Project funding requirements are not outputs of the Control Costs process and
cannot be updated without a change request.
- **B Activity duration estimates**
Incorrect. Activity duration estimates are not outputs of the Control Costs process and
cannot be updated without a change request.
- **C Cost performance baseline**
Incorrect. Cost performance baseline is not an output of the Control Costs process and
cannot be updated without a change request.
- **D Cost forecasts**
Correct. Cost forecasts in the form of EAC or bottom-up EAC are outputs of the Control
Costs process.

Which of the following is an output of the Estimate Activity Durations process?

Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Estimate Activity Durations process has the following three outputs:
● Duration estimates
● Basis of estimates

---

● Project documents updates

**Details for Each Option:**

Activity Durations process in the PMBOK® Guide.

Incorrect. Work performance data are measurements and observations collected during
project execution. The Estimate Activity Durations process is in the Planning Process
Group, not the Executing Process Group; therefore, work performance data would not yet
be available making this answer incorrect.

Question 84 of 210
Question ID: 651663
Which of the following is a tool or technique used in the Develop Project Charter process?
Top of Form
- **A Project management information system (PMIS)**
- **B Conflict management**
- **C Trend analysis**
- **D Needs assessment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Project charters usually involve the input of several stakeholders.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Develop Project Charter is the process of developing a document that formally authorizes
the existence of a project and provides the project manager with the authority to apply
organizational resources to project activities. This process has the four following tools and
techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering
● Interpersonal and team skills (e.g., conflict management)
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project management information system (PMIS)**

---

Incorrect. While a project management information system is a tool and technique used in
many processes, it is not used in the Develop Project Charter process.
- **B Conflict management**
Correct. Conflict management is an example of interpersonal and team skills which is a
tool and technique used in the Develop Project Charter process. Conflict management can
be used to help bring stakeholders into alignment on various elements of the charter.
- **C Trend analysis**
Incorrect. Trend analysis is a data analysis tool and technique that uses mathematical
models to forecast future outcomes based on historical results. Neither trend analysis nor
data analysis is used in the Develop Project Charter process.
- **D Needs assessment**
Incorrect. A needs assessment often precedes the business case and is considered
pre-project work. A needs assessment is not a tool or technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 75, 80

Question 85 of 210
Question ID: 651545

---

Which of the following is an input to the Monitor and Control Project Work process?
Top of Form
- **A Approved change requests**
- **B Change requests**
- **C Work performance information**
- **D Accepted deliverables**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is an input to the Monitor and Control Project Work process only.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Monitor and Control Project Work process is the process of tracking, reviewing, and
reporting overall progress to meet the performance objectives defined in the project management
plan. It has the following six inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Work performance Information
● Agreements
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Approved change requests**
Incorrect. Approved change requests are inputs to the Direct and Manage Project Work,
Control Quality, and Control Procurements processes. They are not inputs to the Monitor
and Control Project Work process.
- **B Change requests**

---

Incorrect. Change requests are inputs to the Perform Integrated Change Control process.
They are not inputs to the Monitor and Control Project Work process.
- **C Work performance information**
Correct. Work performance information is an input to the Monitor and Control Project
Work process.
- **D Accepted deliverables**
Incorrect. Accepted deliverables are inputs to the Close Project or Phase process. They are
not inputs to the Monitor and Control Project Work process.

Question 86 of 210
Question ID: 626028
Throughout the project, the stakeholders have been raising various problems, gaps,
inconsistencies, and conflicts.
Which of the following should be used to capture this information?
Top of Form

---

- **A Change log**
- **B Risk register**
- **C Issue log**
- **D Stakeholder register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which is the output of the Direct and Manage Project Work process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The problems, gaps, inconsistencies, and conflicts are collectively known as issues. Issues are
recorded in the issue log. The issue log is created as an output of the Direct and Manage Project
Work process as a place to document problems, gaps, inconsistencies, or conflicts that occur
unexpectedly and may threaten the project objectives. Data on issues may include the issue type,
issue originator, description, priority, issue owner, target resolution date, status, final solution,
etc. Issues should be proactively monitored and tracked, and their status communicated to
stakeholders.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change log**
Incorrect. The change log is a comprehensive list of changes submitted during the project
and their current status. While the problems, gaps, inconsistencies, and conflicts may lead
to a change request, those items on their own are not considered change requests and
therefore would not be captured in the change log.
- **B Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a document in which the results of risk analysis and risk
response planning are recorded. Some (but not all) of the problems, gaps, inconsistencies,
and conflicts can be categorized as risks or lead to the identification of new risks.

---

- **C Issue log**
Correct. The issue log is a project document used to document and monitor the problems,
gaps, inconsistencies, and conflicts which are collectively known as issues.
- **D Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document that includes the identification,
assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. This document does not contain
information about the problems, gaps, inconsistencies, and conflicts encountered during the
project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96
Bottom of Form

Question ID: 651585
Which of the following is not an input to the Control Costs process?
Top of Form
- **A Teaming agreements**

---

- **B Project funding requirements**
- **C Project management plan**
- **D Work performance data**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Control Costs process is used to monitor the status of the project to update the project
budget and managing changes to the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Control Costs process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan (primarily the cost management plan, cost baseline, and performance
measurement baseline)
● Project funding requirements
● Project documents (primarily lessons learned register)
● Work performance data
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Teaming agreements**
Correct. Teaming agreements are not an input to the Control Costs process.
- **B Project funding requirements**
Incorrect. Project funding requirements are inputs to the Control Costs process and provide
the information about when funds will be available to cover the project costs.
- **C Project management plan**
Incorrect. Project management plan is an input to the Control Costs process. Primarily the
cost management plan, cost baseline, and performance measurement baseline are used to
understand what the planned costs are.

---

- **D Work performance data**
Incorrect. Work performance data are inputs to the Control Costs process to provide
information on the current costs.

Question 88 of 210
Question ID: 651517
During the activities performed to carry out project work, observations and measurements are
recorded and then become an input to all of the following processes except:
Top of Form
- **A Perform Integrated Change Control**
- **B Monitor Communications**
- **C Validate Scope**
- **D Control Quality**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What do you call observations and measurements recorded during activities being performed to
carry out project work?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Direct and Manage Project Work process is the process of leading and performing the work
defined in the project management plan and implementing approved changes to achieve the
project's objectives. It has the following seven outputs:
● Deliverables
● Work performance data
● Issue log

---

● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project document updates
● Organizational process assets updates
The Direct and Manage Project Work process is the 'only' process that has work performance
data as an output. Work performance data is then used, as an input, in all the Monitoring and
Controlling processes 'except' the Perform Integrated Change Control process and the Monitor
and Control Project Work process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Perform Integrated Change Control**
Correct. Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements recorded
during activities being performed to carry out project work. Therefore, work performance
data are outputs from the Direct and Manage Project Work process. Work performance
data then become inputs to all the controlling processes 'except' the Perform Integrated
Change Control and Monitor and Control Project Work processes.
- **B Monitor Communications**
Incorrect. Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements recorded
during activities being performed to carry out project work. Therefore, work performance
data are outputs from the Direct and Manage Project Work process. Work performance
data then become inputs to various controlling processes such as the Monitor
Communications process.
- **C Validate Scope**
Incorrect. Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements recorded
during activities being performed to carry out project work. Therefore, work performance
data are outputs from the Direct and Manage Project Work process. Work performance
data then become inputs to various controlling processes such as the Validate Scope
process.
- **D Control Quality**
Incorrect. Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements recorded
during activities being performed to carry out project work. Therefore, work performance
data are outputs from the Direct and Manage Project Work process. Work performance
data then become inputs to various controlling processes such as the Control Quality
process.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 90-91, 95

Question ID: 651551
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Collect Requirements process?
Top of Form
- **A Project charter**
- **B Alternative analysis**
- **C Inspection**
- **D Interviews**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Collect Requirements is the process of defining and documenting stakeholders' needs to meet the
project objectives.

---

Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Collect Requirements process has the following tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering (brainstorming, interviews, focus groups, questionnaires and surveys, and
benchmarking)
● Data analysis
● Decision making
● Data representation
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Context diagram
● Prototype
Collect Requirements is the process of determining, documenting, and managing stakeholder
needs and requirements to meet project objectives.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is an input for the Collect Requirements process.
- **B Alternative analysis**
Incorrect. Alternative analysis is a data analysis technique used in the Plan Scope
Management and the Define Scope processes but not the Collect Requirements process,
where the focus is on gathering data and analyzing documents instead of analyzing
alternatives.
- **C Inspection**
Incorrect. An inspection is a tool or technique for Validate Scope and other processes in the
Monitoring and Controlling Process Group.
- **D Interviews**
Correct. As you collect the project requirements, one of the data gathering techniques is to
conduct interviews with stakeholders either individually or in panels by directly asking
prepared and spontaneous questions and recording the responses.

---

Question 90 of 210
Question ID: 651650
Which of the following is not a tool and technique used during the Monitor Risks process?
Top of Form
- **A Technical performance analysis**
- **B Reserve analysis**
- **C Risk audits**
- **D Decision tree analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The trick here is to determine which of the options is not a monitoring or controlling technique.

---

Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Monitor Risks is the process of monitoring the implementation of agreed-upon risk response
plans, tracking identified risks, identifying and analyzing new risks, and evaluating risk process
effectiveness throughout the project. The Monitor Risks process has the following three tools and
techniques:
● Data analysis (including technical performance analysis and reserve analysis)
● Audits (e.g., risk audits)
● Meetings (e.g., risk review meetings)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Technical performance analysis**
Incorrect. Technical performance analysis is a tool and technique employed in the Monitor
Risks process to compare technical accomplishments during project execution to the
schedule of technical achievement.
- **B Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis is a tool and technique employed in the Monitor Risks process
to compare the amount of reserves remaining to the amount of risk remaining to determine
if the reserves are adequate.
- **C Risk audits**
Incorrect. Risk audits are a tool and technique employed in the Monitor Risks process to
consider the effectiveness of the risk management process.
- **D Decision tree analysis**
Correct. Decision tree analysis is a tool and technique employed in the Perform
Quantitative Risk Analysis process to support the selection of the best of several alternative
courses of action. This technique is not used during the Monitor Risks process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 453, 435

Question ID: 651700
Which of the following is an output of the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process?
Top of Form
- **A Stakeholder register**
- **B Risk management plan**
- **C Stakeholder engagement plan**
- **D Change log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the primary purpose of this process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Plan Stakeholder Engagement is the process of developing approaches to involve project
stakeholders based on their needs, expectations, interests, and potential impact on the project.
The single output of this process is the stakeholder engagement plan, which is a component of

---

the project management plan that identifies the strategies and actions required to promote the
productive involvement of the project's stakeholders in both decision making and execution.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is an output of the Identify Stakeholders process and an
input to the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process, but it is not an output.
- **B Risk management plan**
Incorrect. The risk management plan is an output of the Plan Risk Management process
and an input to (not output from) the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **C Stakeholder engagement plan**
Correct. The stakeholder engagement plan is the singular output of the Plan Stakeholder
Engagement process.
- **D Change log**
Incorrect. The change log is an input to the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process but is
not an output.

Question ID: 651590
Which of the following is an input to the Plan Quality Management process?
Top of Form
- **A Contracts**
- **B Stakeholder register**
- **C Resource calendars**
- **D Risk report**

Correct Answer: B

The Plan Quality Management process has the following five inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., stakeholder register)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
Plan Quality Management is the process of identifying quality requirements and/or standards for

Question 93 of 210
Question ID: 651677
What components of the project management plan may encourage iterative practices, such as a
product backlog and a sprint review, to be included in the scope management plan?
Top of Form
- **A Management reviews and the schedule baseline**
- **B The project life cycle description and development approach**
- **C The requirements management plan and the project charter**
- **D The quality management plan and the cost management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

To answer this question properly, you need to be able to recognize the components of the project
management plan, and the flow of using such components in relation to scope management.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scope management plan is a component of the project or program management plan that
describes how the scope will be defined, developed, monitored, controlled, and validated. The
development of the scope management plan begins with the analysis of information contained in
the project charter, the latest approved subsidiary plans of the project management plan, as well
as EEFs and OPAs. However, the question is asking specifically for components of the project
management plan, which rules out items that are not project management plan components.
Then, you must narrow the choices to components that may drive the use of iterative practices
such as a product backlog and a sprint review. Of the project management plan components
shown, the project life cycle description and the development approach are most influential
regarding iterative practices in scope management.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Management reviews and the schedule baseline**

---

Incorrect. Indeed, management reviews are a project management plan component that
identifies the points in the project when stakeholders review progress to determine if
performance is as expected. Management reviews might be likened to sprint reviews and
therefore encourage such a practice. However, the schedule baseline uses the scope
management plan as an input, not the other way around.
- **B The project life cycle description and development approach**
Correct. Both the project life cycle description and the development approach are
components of the project management plan that serve as inputs to the Plan Scope
Management process. Furthermore, they both determine the series of phases in the project
and whether iterative practices such as product backlogs and sprint reviews are
appropriate.
- **C The requirements management plan and the project charter**
Incorrect. The requirements management plan is certainly an output of the Plan Scope
Management process. However, the project charter is not a component of the project
management plan.
- **D The quality management plan and the cost management plan**
Incorrect. Indeed, the quality management plan and the cost management plan are both
components of the project management plan. And the organization's quality policies,
methodologies, and standards certainly influence the way project and product scope will be
managed. However, only the quality management plan is explicitly an input to the Plan
Scope Management process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 135, 131

Question 94 of 210
Question ID: 651563
Which of the following is an output of the Sequence Activities process?
Top of Form
- **A Work performance data**
- **B Project schedule network diagrams**
- **C Project scope statement**
- **D Activity list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Sequence Activities is the process of identifying and documenting relationships among the
project activities which can be displayed graphically.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Sequence Activities process is where relationships among the project activities are identified
and documented. The process has the following two outputs:
● Project schedule network diagrams
● Project documents updates (e.g., activity list)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance data**
Incorrect. Work performance data is the raw observations and measurements identified
during the execution of project activities. Sequence Activities is a planning process, not an

---

execution process; therefore, work performance data is not an output of the Sequence
Activities process.
- **B Project schedule network diagrams**
Correct. A project schedule network diagram is a graphical representation of the logical
relationships among the project schedule activities and is an output of the Sequence
Activities process.
- **C Project scope statement**
Incorrect. The project scope statement is the description of the project scope, major
deliverables, assumptions, and constraints. The project scope statement is an input to the
Sequence Activities process as part of the scope baseline and not an output of the process.
- **D Activity list**
Incorrect. The activity list is an example of the project documents that are inputs to the
Sequence Activities process. During the Sequence Activities process, the activity list may be
impacted leading to an update. Therefore, it is the 'updated' activity list that is an output of
the Sequence Activity process, not the activity list.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 187, 194

This project document is used throughout the project life cycle.

- **C Constraints log**
Incorrect. 'Constraints log' is a fake term made up for this question.
- **D Agreements**
Incorrect. Agreements are inputs to the Develop Project Charter process, not an output.

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 97 of 210
Question ID: 651536
Using the decision matrix shown below, what is the EMV for the upgrade option?

---

Top of Form
- **A $36M**
- **B $46M**
- **C $70M**
- **D $10M**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Remember to take into account all of the paths for the selected option.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Decision trees are used to support the selection of the best of several alternative courses of
action. Typically, the option or branch with the highest calculated expected monetary value
(EMV). To calculate the branch EMV, the payoff minus costs are calculated for each path within

---

the option. In this example, that would be $70M for the Upgrade Plant, Strong demand path
($70M = $120M - $50M), and $10M for the Upgrade Plant, Weak Demand path ($10M = $60M
- $50M). Then each path value is multiplied by the probability of the path, and all path values are
summed. For the Upgrade/Strong Demand path the result is $42M ($42M = $70M x 0.60), and
the Upgrade/Weak Demand path result is $4M ($4M = $10M x .040). When the two are added,
the resulting EMV for the Upgrade Plant option is $46M.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A $36M**
Incorrect. $36M is the EMV for the 'Build New Plant' option.
- **B $46M**
Correct. $46M is the sum of the Upgrade/Strong Demand path EMV ($42M) and the
Upgrade/Weak Demand path ($4M).
- **C $70M**
Incorrect. $70M is the 'Upgrade Plant/Strong Demand' path payoff minus costs ($70M =
$120M - $50M).
- **D $10M**
Incorrect. $10M is the 'Upgrade Plant/Weak Demand' path payoff minus costs ($10M =
$60M - $50M).

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 435
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 98 of 210
Question ID: 651623
Which tool or technique used during the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process helps the
project manager understand the strategies of the organization and determine who wields power
and influence?
Top of Form
- **A Networking**
- **B Political awareness**
- **C Active listening**
- **D Multicriteria decision analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This question is really about understanding influence and power.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Political awareness is a powerful technique that concerns the recognition of formal and informal
power relationships, and the willingness to operate within these relationships. An understanding
of the strategies of the organization, knowing who wields power and influence, and developing
an ability to communicate with key stakeholders are all aspects of this technique.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Networking**
Incorrect. Networking ensures access to information about levels of stakeholder
engagement. It is not the tool and technique described in the question.
- **B Political awareness**
Correct. Political awareness is a tool and technique employed during the Monitor
Stakeholder Engagement process that helps the project manager understand the
organization's strategies and determine who wields power.
- **C Active listening**
Incorrect. Active listening is used to reduce misunderstandings and other
miscommunication. It is not the tool and technique described in the question.
- **D Multicriteria decision analysis**
Incorrect. Multicriteria decision analysis is a technique that prioritizes and weighs criteria
for successful stakeholder engagement to identify the most appropriate choices. It is not the
tool and technique described in the question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 530, 534, 376

Question ID: 651631
Which of the following is an output of the Identify Risks process?
Top of Form
- **A Activity duration estimates**
- **B Scope baseline**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Project schedule network diagrams**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Focus on the primary purpose of the Identify Risks process.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Identify Risks is the process of identifying individual risks as well as sources of overall risk and
documenting their characteristics. This process has three outputs:
● Risk register
● Risk report
● Project documents updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Activity duration estimates**
Incorrect. Activity duration estimates are outputs of the Estimate Activity Durations
process. They are not outputs of the Identify Risks process.

approved changes to the scope baseline are referred to as 'project documents updates'. The
scope baseline is not an output of the Identify Risks process.
- **C Risk register**
Correct. The risk register is the primary output of the Identify Risks process. It is where all
the risks and associated information identified during this process are recorded.
- **D Project schedule network diagrams**
Incorrect. Project schedule network diagrams are outputs from the Sequence Activities
process. They are not outputs of the Identify Risks process.

Question ID: 651550
Which of the following is an output of the Collect Requirements process?
Top of Form

---

- **A Change requests**
- **B Deliverables**
- **C Requirements documentation**
- **D Stakeholder register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Collect Requirements is the process of defining and documenting stakeholders' needs to meet the
project objectives.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Collect Requirements is the process of determining, documenting, and managing
stakeholder needs and requirements to meet project objectives. This process has the following
two outputs:
● Requirements documentation
● Requirements traceability matrix

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests may be created to adjust a baselined scope or project
management plan component but are not explicitly listed as an output of the Collect
Requirements process. Remember, the scope has not yet been baselined during this process.
- **B Deliverables**
Incorrect. Deliverables are the final products, services, and results that are ready for your
quality control processes to validate and for customers to accept. However, deliverables are
not produced while you are still collecting requirements during the Planning Process
Group.

---

- **C Requirements documentation**
Correct. The process of collecting requirements produces documentation that may take
many forms to describe how individual requirements meet the business need for the project,
and how they may be measured and tested, traced, complete, consistent, and acceptable to
stakeholders.
- **D Stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is not explicitly listed as an output of the Collect
Requirements process but serves as an input project document of the process.

Question 101 of 210
Question ID: 651519
During the past few weeks, there have been many changes to the project deliverables and the
project manager is not sure which changes add real business value.
Which of the following could the project manager use to evaluate the impact that changes may
have on the project objectives?
Top of Form

---

- **A Change log**
- **B Requirements log**
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
- **D Business case**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of the item that links requirements with business and project objectives.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Serving as an output of the Collect Requirements process, the requirements traceability matrix is
a grid that links product requirements from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. The
implementation of a requirements traceability matrix helps ensure that each requirement adds
business value by linking it to the business and project objectives. It provides a means to track
requirements throughout the project life cycle, helping to ensure that requirements approved in
the requirements documentation are delivered at the end of the project. Finally, it provides a
structure for managing changes to the product scope.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change log**
Incorrect. The change log is a comprehensive list of changes made during the project.
- **B Requirements log**
Incorrect. The requirements log is not a project document explicitly listed in the PMBOK®
Guide.
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
Correct. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links each product requirement
from an original business need to the deliverable(s) that should satisfy each requirement.

---

As an input to the Validate Scope process, this matrix can be used to detect the impact of
changes on project objectives.
- **D Business case**
Incorrect. The business case is a documented economic feasibility study used to establish
the validity of the benefits of a selected component.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 148-149

Question ID: 651646
Which of the following is not an input to the Implement Risk Responses process?
Top of Form
- **A Project team assignments**
- **B Risk management plan**

---

- **C Risk report**
- **D Lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Implement Risk Responses is the process of implementing agreed-upon risk response plans.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Implement Risk Responses is the process of implementing agreed-upon risk response plans.
Implement Risk Responses is the process of implementing agreed-upon risk response plans. It
has the following three inputs:
● Project management plan (e.g., the risk management plan)
● Project documents (including the lessons learned register, the risk register, and the risk report)
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project team assignments**
Correct. Project team assignments are not an input to the Implement Risk Responses
process. Updates to project team assignments are outputs from this process.
- **B Risk management plan**
Incorrect. The risk management plan is an input of the Implement Risk Responses process,
where it provides the roles and responsibilities of team members and other stakeholders, as
well as the level of detail for the risk management methodology and the project's risk
thresholds.
- **C Risk report**
Incorrect. The risk report is an input to the Implement Risk Responses process. It includes
an assessment of the current overall project risk exposure, the agreed-upon risk response
strategy, and the identified individual project risks with their planned responses.
- **D Lessons learned register**

---

Incorrect. The lessons learned register is an input to the Implement Risk Responses process,
where it provides lessons learned about risk responses that were implemented earlier in the
project.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 103 of 210
Question ID: 651534
What is the purpose of resource calendars?
Top of Form
- **A Resource calendars are created during the Develop Team process to show when team members**
can participate in team development activities.
- **B Resource calendars are outputs of the Acquire Resources process to show when team members**
are available to perform project activities.
- **C When estimating activity resources, you create resource calendars to present the resource**
availability in the form of a histogram.

---

- **D Resource calendars track when you are assigned to the project but do not account for**
commitments to other projects.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Eliminate any choice that includes something that is not true about resource calendars.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The resource calendars identify the working days and shifts when each specific resource is
available. After you acquire the project team, you are ready to document the time periods when
each team member is available to work on the project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Resource calendars are created during the Develop Team process to show when team**
members can participate in team development activities.
Incorrect. For the Develop Team process, resource calendars serve as a project document
input and a project document update output. Team development does not create resource
calendars but merely updates them. Furthermore, resource calendars are not solely focused
on availability for team development activities, but project work.
- **B Resource calendars are outputs of the Acquire Resources process to show when team**
members are available to perform project activities.
Correct. Resource calendars are outputs of the Acquire Resources and show a team
member's availability to do project work.
- **C When estimating activity resources, you create resource calendars to present the resource**
availability in the form of a histogram.
Incorrect. A resource histogram is a common visual tool to manage resource allocation but
is not explicitly listed outside the glossary and is a separate artifact from the resource
calendar. However, resource calendars serve as an input project document for the Estimate
Activity Resources process, which does not explicitly list the resource calendar as an
output.
- **D Resource calendars track when you are assigned to the project but do not account for**
commitments to other projects.

---

Incorrect. A resource calendar should account for an individual's constraints and
availability (or lack thereof), so it is relevant to track time allocated as holidays, vacation
days, non-working days, as well as commitments to other projects.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 334, 323, 331

Question 104 of 210
Question ID: 612503
Which of the following is not an input to the Identify Risks process?
Top of Form
- **A Cost management plan**
- **B Scope management plan**
- **C Schedule management plan**
- **D Quality management plan**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What constraints may introduce risk to the project?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The cost management plan, the schedule management plan, and the quality management plan are
all inputs to the Identify Risks process. Of the choices provided, only the scope management
plan is not an input to the Identify Risks process and is, therefore, the best answer to the question
asked. Note, the scope baseline is an input to the Identify Risks process because it includes
deliverables and criteria for their acceptance, some of which might introduce risk. However, the
scope baseline is not part of the scope management plan. The scope baseline is part of the project
management plan which includes the subsidiary plans, such as the scope management plan, the
baselines, such as the scope baseline, and some other components.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cost management plan**
Incorrect. The cost management plan will help identify areas of uncertainty associated with
costs within the project.
- **B Scope management plan**
Correct. The scope management plan is not listed in the PMBOK® Guide as an input
document in the Identify Risks process described in this question.
- **C Schedule management plan**
Incorrect. The schedule management plan would be needed as it could point to uncertainty
in project schedule that may introduce risk to the project.
- **D Quality management plan**
Incorrect. The quality management plan is an input in the Identify Risks process. It
establishes how quality policies, methodologies, and standards are implemented in the
project. The plan may serve to identify areas that are subject to uncertainty or ambiguity, or
where key assumptions have been made that might give rise to risk.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 409, 87

Which of the following is an output of the Identify Stakeholders process?

Question answered incorrectly

Which choice is most directly related to the work of the Identify Stakeholders process?
Correct Answer: C

---


**Explanation:**

Identify Stakeholders is the process of identifying project stakeholders regularly and analyzing
and documenting relevant information regarding their interests, involvement, interdependencies,
influence, and potential impact on project success. The Identify Stakeholders process has the
following four outputs:
● Stakeholder register
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates

stakeholders to various roles and activities, but the calendars are not outputs of the Identify
Stakeholders process.

process because this register contains the key information about identified stakeholders.
- **D Quality metrics**

processes, but they are not an output of the identify Stakeholders process.

Question ID: 651608
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Manage Team process?

- **B Work performance reports**
- **C Expert judgment**
- **D Communication technology**
Question answered incorrectly

What would help you perform activities related to the Manage Team process, namely tracking
team member performance, providing feedback, resolving issues, and managing changes?
Correct Answer: A

resolving issues, and managing team changes to optimize project performance. The Manage
Team process has the following two tools and techniques:

---

● Interpersonal and team skills (conflict management, decision making, emotional intelligence,

● Project management information system

Question 107 of 210
Question ID: 651385
As a project manager, you are developing a resource management plan for your software
development project, and you need to find a way to document and communicate the detailed
descriptions of the team members' roles and responsibilities.
What tool will best meet your needs?
Top of Form
- **A Role-responsibility-authority form**
- **B RACI chart**
- **C Resource breakdown structure**
- **D Hierarchical chart**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice accurately describes a data representation technique that might be used as
part of the Plan Resource Management process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Plan Resource Management process is underway. Data
representation techniques that may be used for this process include charts. Various formats exist
to document and communicate team member roles and responsibilities, but most fall into
hierarchical, matrix, or text-oriented formats. A hierarchical format may be used to represent
high-level roles, while a text-based format may be better suited to document the detailed team
member responsibilities. Text-oriented documents provide detailed information such as
responsibilities, authority, competencies, and qualifications. These documents are known by
various names including position descriptions and role-responsibility-authority forms. Since the
question is asking to find a way to document and communicate the 'detailed' descriptions of the

---

team members' roles and responsibilities, using a role-responsibility-authority form is the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Role-responsibility-authority form**
Correct. A role-responsibility-authority form is an example of a text-oriented format that
can be used as a data representation technique to specify the team members' roles and
responsibilities that require detailed descriptions.
- **B RACI chart**
Incorrect. A RACI chart is a common type of responsibility assignment matrix that uses
responsible, accountable, consult, and inform statuses to define the involvement of
stakeholders in project activities. Although a RACI chart may be used to document project
roles and responsibilities, a RACI chart is a high-level representation matrix that does not
provide detailed descriptions.
- **C Resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. A resource breakdown structure is an example of the hierarchical format which
is typically used to represent resources in a high-level, while the question is asking for a
tool that shows the detailed descriptions.
- **D Hierarchical chart**
Incorrect. A hierarchical format may be used to represent high-level roles of team
members, while a text-based format may be better suited to document the detailed
responsibilities. Thus, hierarchical charts are not likely to used to document detailed
responsibilities.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 316-317
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 108 of 210
Question ID: 651503
All of the following are included in the scope baseline except:
Top of Form
- **A Project scope statement**
- **B Work breakdown structure**
- **C WBS dictionary**
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the choices is used to track completeness throughout the project lifecycle it is not a part
of the scope baseline.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scope baseline is a principal output of the Create WBS process. It encompasses the approved
version of a scope statement, work breakdown structure (WBS), and its associated WBS
dictionary. A baseline can be changed only through formal change control procedures and is used
as a basis for comparison during Monitoring and Controlling. In contrast, the requirements
traceability matrix is a project document that serves as an output of the Collect Requirements
process. The requirements traceability matrix is used to link each requirement with the
deliverables that should fulfill the requirement. Unlike the scope baseline, this matrix needs to be

---

updated throughout both the Execution and the Monitoring and Controlling process groups as the
project progresses and the status of the requirement fulfillment changes.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project scope statement**
Incorrect. The project scope statement is an important part of the scope baseline. It
describes the project scope, along with major deliverables and assumptions.
- **B Work breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The WBS is a part of the scope baseline that decomposes the project scope of
work into smaller and manageable components.
- **C WBS dictionary**
Incorrect. To document the details of deliverable requirements and associated activities for
each WBS component, the WBS dictionary is part of the scope baseline, which may only be
changed through a formal change control process.
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Correct. Unlike the scope baseline, the requirements traceability matrix is subject to
frequent updates throughout the project life cycle as each deliverable makes progress to
fulfilling the requirements.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 161, 148-149

Question ID: 651667
Which of the following is a tool or technique used in the Manage Project Knowledge process?
Top of Form
- **A Problem solving**
- **B Information management**
- **C Data analysis**
- **D Historical information review**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the goals of the Manage Project Knowledge process is to contribute to organizational
learning.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Manage Project Knowledge Manage is the process of using existing knowledge and creating
new knowledge to achieve the project's objectives and contribute to organizational learning. This
process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Knowledge management
● Information management
● Interpersonal and team skills

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Problem solving**
Incorrect. Problem solving is not a tool or technique used in the Manage Project
Knowledge process.
- **B Information management**
Correct. Information management is a series of tools and techniques used to create and
connect people to information. They are useful for sharing simple, unambiguous, codified
explicit knowledge. Information management is a tool and technique used in the Manage
Project Knowledge process.
- **C Data analysis**
Incorrect. Data analysis is not a tool or technique used in the Manage Project Knowledge
process.
- **D Historical information review**
Incorrect. A historical information review is a tool and technique used in the Determine
Budget process only. It is not used in the Manage Project Knowledge process.

Question 110 of 210
Question ID: 651576
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Control Schedule process?
Top of Form
- **A Organizational process assets (OPAs)**
- **B Performance reviews**
- **C Meetings**
- **D Expert judgment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Control Schedule is the process of monitoring and controlling the schedule baseline.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Control Schedule process is where project status is monitored to update the project schedule
and manage changes to the schedule baseline. It has the following six tools and techniques:
● Data analysis (e.g., performance reviews)
● Critical path method
● Project management information system
● Resource optimization
● Leads and lags
● Schedule compression

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Organizational process assets (OPAs)**
Incorrect. OPAs are not a tool or technique; they are typically inputs to a process.

---

- **B Performance reviews**
Correct. Performance reviews are an example of a data analysis technique where schedule
performance is measured, compared, and analyzed against the schedule baseline.
Performance reviews are part of the tools and techniques used in the Control Schedule
process.
- **C Meetings**
Incorrect. While meetings are a common tool and technique in project management
processes, the PMBOK® Guide does not list meetings as tools and techniques in the
Control Schedule process.
- **D Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is not listed in the PMBOK® Guide as a tool and technique in
the Control Schedule process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 222, 227

Question 111 of 210
Question ID: 651533

---

Which of the following is an example of a result of the Determine Budget process?
Top of Form
- **A $100,000 is required by the project on a quarterly basis.**
- **B The services of a trusted shredding company are required every month to handle sensitive paper**
documents.
- **C The project is going to follow a similar structure as a similar implementation project previously**
undertaken by the organization.
- **D A signed agreement with a financial institution will be provided to finance the project.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of how each of the choices is related to the Determine Budget process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Determine Budget process has the following outputs: cost baseline, project funding
requirements, and project document updates (namely project schedule, cost estimates, and risk
register). The correct answer lists quarterly project funding requirements. The rest of the choices
represent different examples of inputs to the Determine Budget process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A $100,000 is required by the project on a quarterly basis.**
Correct. This choice is an example of project funding requirements.
- **B The services of a trusted shredding company are required every month to handle sensitive**
paper documents.
Incorrect. This choice is an example of an assumption that is part of the basis for estimates
and an input rather than an output of the Determine Budget process.

---

- **C The project is going to follow a similar structure as a similar implementation project**
previously undertaken by the organization.
Incorrect. This choice is another example of an assumption that is part of the basis for
estimates and an input rather than an output of the Determine Budget process.
- **D A signed agreement with a financial institution will be provided to finance the project.**
Incorrect. Agreements are useful as an input rather than an output of the Determine Budget
process in order to determine any financing costs that need to be accounted for in the
budget.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 248

Which of the following is not an output of the Control Quality process?

- **B Checklists**

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the answer choices is a tool and technique, not an output.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Control Quality is the process of monitoring and recording results of executing the quality
management activities to assess performance and ensure the project outputs are complete,
correct, and meet customer expectations. The Control Quality process has the following six
outputs:

● Work performance information

● Project documents updates

this choice is the correct answer to the question asked.
- **C Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are outputs of the Control Quality process.

---

- **D Quality control measurements**
Incorrect. Quality control measurements are outputs of the Control Quality process.

Question ID: 651526
Expert judgment is a tool and technique used in all of the following processes except:
Top of Form
- **A Develop Project Charter**
- **B Manage Communications**
- **C Conduct Procurements**
- **D Identify Stakeholders**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of when you would require expertise in a knowledge area, discipline, industry, etc.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Manage Communications is the process of ensuring timely and appropriate collection, creation,
distribution, storage, retrieval, management, monitoring, and the ultimate disposition of project
information. The Manage Communications process has the following seven tools and techniques:
● Communication technology
● Communication methods
● Communication skills
● Project management information system
● Project reporting
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Meetings
The PMBOK® Guide does not include expert judgment as a tool and technique under Manage
Communications.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Develop Project Charter**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is used in the Develop Project Charter process to get the
appropriate technical and managerial details into the project charter.
- **B Manage Communications**
Correct. Manage Communications is part of the Executing Process Group. When
conducting communications, expert judgment is not used. Expert judgment is used in the
Monitor Communications process.
- **C Conduct Procurements**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is used in the Conduct Procurements process. It is typically
needed to evaluate proposals.
- **D Identify Stakeholders**

---

Incorrect. Expert judgment is used in the Identify Stakeholders process to ensure all
stakeholders have been identified, listed, and assessed appropriately.

Question 114 of 210
Question ID: 651697
Which of the following is not an output of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process?
Top of Form
- **A Updates to the stakeholder register**
- **B Updates to the stakeholder engagement plan**
- **C Updates to the communications management plan**
- **D Meetings**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

Which answer stands out from the rest?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Manage Stakeholder Engagement is the process of communicating and working with
stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations, address issues, and foster appropriate
stakeholder involvement. There are three outputs of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement
process:
● Change results
● Project management plan updates (including the communications management plan and the
stakeholder engagement plan)
● Project documents updates (including the change log, the issue log, the lessons learned register,
and the stakeholder register)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Updates to the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register updates are outputs of the Manage Stakeholder
Engagement process. The stakeholder register is updated based on new information
provided to stakeholders about resolved issues, approved changes, and general project
status.
- **B Updates to the stakeholder engagement plan**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement plan updates are outputs of the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement process where the stakeholder engagement plan is updated to
reflect new or changed management strategies required to engage stakeholders effectively.
- **C Updates to the communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan updates are outputs of the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement process. The communications management plan is updated to
reflect new or changed stakeholder requirements.
- **D Meetings**
Correct. Meetings are techniques used during the Manage Stakeholder Engagement
process and not outputs of the process.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 523, 528-529

Question 115 of 210
Question ID: 651683
Which of the following is not one of the tools and techniques for the Acquire Resources process?
Top of Form
- **A Negotiation**
- **B Pre-assignment**
- **C Virtual teams**
- **D Decision tree analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Remember, you’re looking for a choice that would not be helpful in obtaining team members or
physical resources for the project.

---

Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Acquire Resources process has the following four tools and techniques:
● Decision making (multi-criteria decision analysis)
● Interpersonal and team skills (negotiation)
● Pre-assignment
● Virtual teams
In the context of acquiring resources, multicriteria decision analysis serves as the
decision-making technique. Using a decision matrix to systematically evaluate several
characteristics (such as availability, cost, features, experience, knowledge, skills) shared among
the choices, you then rank the choices by the resulting mathematical scores. In the context of
quantifying risks, the decision tree analysis uses a diagram and specific formulas to evaluate the
impact of a chain of multiple options for the purpose of prioritizing risks and their responses.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Negotiation**
Incorrect. An interpersonal and team skill that can be used for the Acquire Resources
process includes but is not limited to negotiation. Many projects need to negotiate for the
required resources.
- **B Pre-assignment**
Incorrect. Pre-assignment is a tool for the Acquire Resources process. The physical or team
resources may be determined in advance if specified in the project charter, or if the project
is dependent upon the expertise of particular persons.
- **C Virtual teams**
Incorrect. The use of virtual teams supported by communication technology creates new
possibilities when acquiring project team members to hire specialized experts who are not
in the same location as most of the team.
- **D Decision tree analysis**
Correct. This data analysis technique is one of several used in the Perform Quantitative
Risk Analysis process, not the Acquire Resources process. A decision tree analysis is a

---

diagramming and calculation technique to evaluate the impact of a chain of multiple
options in the presence of uncertainty.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 332-333

Question 116 of 210
Question ID: 651684
Which of the following data analysis techniques would be best for determining the resources
needed at upcoming stages of the project and to see if performance has been improving or
deteriorating over time?
Top of Form
- **A Cost-benefit analysis**
- **B Trend analysis**
- **C Performance reviews**
- **D Project management information system (PMIS)**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This question describes conditions that occur in the Control Resources process. Remember, you
are looking for a technique for analyzing data on resources and performance over time.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Trend analysis is a data analysis technique for several processes in the Monitoring and
Controlling process group. In the Control Resources process, the project team may use trend
analysis on current performance information to determine the resources needed at upcoming
stages of the project. Trend analysis examines project performance over time and can be used to
determine whether performance is improving or deteriorating.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cost-benefit analysis**
Incorrect. A cost-benefit analysis is a data analysis technique to determine the best
corrective actions in case of project deviations discovered during the Control Resources
process. However, this technique does not help forecast needs or trends.
- **B Trend analysis**
Correct. In the Control Resources process, the project team may use trend analysis based
on current performance information to forecast resource needs and report improvement or
deterioration over time.
- **C Performance reviews**
Incorrect. Performance reviews are considered a data analysis technique for controlling
resources by pinpointing variances from expected performance and utilization. However,
performance reviews do not help forecast needs or trends.
- **D Project management information system (PMIS)**
Incorrect. A PMIS is a tool used in the Control Resources process but is not a data analysis
technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 356-357

---

Question ID: 651626
The Manage Communications process has seven tools and techniques, including:
● Communication technology
● Communication skills
● Project management information system
● Performance reporting
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Meetings
Which of the following tools and techniques is missing from the list?
Top of Form
- **A Communication methods**
- **B Communication competence**
- **C Project communications**
- **D Recognition and rewards**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Sharing information with stakeholders can include interactive communication, push
communication, and pull communication.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Manage Communications is the process of ensuring timely and appropriate collection, creation,
distribution, storage, retrieval, management, monitoring, and the ultimate disposition of project
information. The Manage Communications process has the following seven tools and techniques:
● Communication technology
● Communication methods
● Communication skills (e.g., communication competence)
● Project management information system
● Performance reporting
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communication methods**
Correct. Communication methods classify the different approaches used to distribute the
project communications. Communication method is a tool/technique used in the Manage
Communications process and is the missing item from the list in the question.
- **B Communication competence**
Incorrect. Communication competence is one of the techniques the PMBOK® Guide
includes in the communications skills tool and technique. Since communications skills are
already listed in the question, this answer is not the correct choice.
- **C Project communications**
Incorrect. Project communications are outputs from the Manage Communications process,
not a tool and technique.
- **D Recognition and rewards**

---

Incorrect. Recognition and rewards belong under the tool and technique used in the
Develop Team process, not the Manage Communications process.

Question 118 of 210
Question ID: 651524
Which of the following tools or techniques is used by buyers during the Control Procurements
process to verify the compliance of the seller's deliverables to the contract?
Top of Form
- **A Audits**
- **B Inspections**
- **C Checklist analysis**
- **D Bidder conferences**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The buyer is examining the work product rather than work processes.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Control Procurements is the process of managing procurement relationships, monitoring contract
performance, making changes and corrections as appropriate, and closing out contracts. The
process has the following five tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Claims administration
● Data analysis
● Inspections
● Audits

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Audits**
Incorrect. Audits are structured reviews of the processes used during the Control
Procurements process and are not specific to the deliverables.
- **B Inspections**
Correct. Inspections are structured reviews of either the deliverables or a review of the
work itself to verify the work complies with the contract. Inspections are techniques used
during the Control Procurements process.
- **C Checklist analysis**
Incorrect. Checklist analysis is a technique for systematically reviewing materials using a
list for accuracy and completeness. The PMBOK® Guide does not include checklist
analysis as a tool or technique used in the Control Procurements process.
- **D Bidder conferences**
Incorrect. A bidder conference is one of the tools and techniques used during the Conduct
Procurement process, which precedes the Control Procurement process.

**Reference:**

Question 119 of 210
Question ID: 651602
Which of the following is an input to the Acquire Resources process?
Top of Form
- **A Stakeholder management plan**
- **B Pre-assignment**
- **C Activity cost estimates**
- **D Enterprise environmental factors**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Acquire Resources is the first Project Resource Management process of the Executing Process
Group, so you should have baselines available that help prepare to select resources and assign
them to their respective activities.

---

Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Acquire Resources is the process of obtaining team members, facilities, equipment, materials,
supplies, and other resources necessary to complete project work. The Acquire Resources
process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan (resource management plan, procurement management plan and cost
baselines)
● Project documents
● EEFs (costs, availability, locations, competence levels, experience, market conditions,
organizational structure)
● OPAs

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Stakeholder management plan**
Incorrect. Of the project management plan components, the resource management plan and
procurement management plan and cost baseline are explicitly listed as input for acquiring
resources, not the stakeholder management plan.
- **B Pre-assignment**
Incorrect. The physical or team resources may be determined in advance if specified in the
project charter, or if the project is dependent upon the expertise of particular persons.
However, pre-assignment is a tool for the Acquire Resources process, not an input.
- **C Activity cost estimates**
Incorrect. Cost estimates are not a direct input to the Acquire Resources process. Instead,
the cost baseline provides the overall budget for the project activities.
- **D Enterprise environmental factors**
Correct. The EEFs that may be helpful for this process include the costs, availability,
locations, competence levels, and experience of resources to be acquired and assigned as
well as your organizational structure and marketplace conditions.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 330-331

Question 120 of 210
Question ID: 651518
The financial business analyst of an initial public offering (IPO) project meets with the
stakeholders to agree on how business requirements will be documented.
What is the expected result of this meeting?
Top of Form
- **A Updates to the requirements management plan**
- **B Updates to the business analysis plan**
- **C Updates to the requirements documentation**
- **D Updates to the stakeholder register**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

Think about which choice is the most relevant output of the Plan Scope Management process with
relation to the objective of the meeting.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

In this context, the requirements management plan is the most relevant outcome of the meeting
described in the question. A critical output of the Plan Scope Management process, the
requirements management plan describes how requirements will be analyzed, documented, and
managed.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Updates to the requirements management plan**
Correct. This component of the project management plan describes how requirements will be
analyzed, documented and managed, which is the subject of the meeting in question.
- **B Updates to the business analysis plan**
Incorrect. The business analysis plan is another word for the requirements management
plan, according to PMI's Business Analysis for Practitioners: A Practice Guide, but in this
sample exam, look for an output of the Plan Scope Management process that is commonly
known and explicitly listed in the PMBOK® Guide, which is the principal reference for this
exam.
- **C Updates to the requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation describes how individual requirements meet the
business need for the project, which was not quite the subject of the meeting in question.
- **D Updates to the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register contains all details related to the identified stakeholders,
which is not relevant to the meeting in question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 137

Question ID: 651621
Which of the following is an output of the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process?
Top of Form
- **A Resource management plan updates**
- **B Project communications**
- **C Change management plan**
- **D Presentations**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager may have to adjust team member responsibilities for stakeholder
engagement activities.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Monitor Stakeholder Engagement is the process of monitoring project stakeholder relationships,
and tailoring strategies for engaging stakeholders through the modification of engagement
strategies and plans. This process has the following four outputs:

---

● Work performance information
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (including the resource management plan, the
communications management plan, and the stakeholder engagement plan)
● Project documents updates (including the issue log, the lessons learned register, the risk register,
and the stakeholder register)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Resource management plan updates**
Correct. Project management plan updates, including updates to the resource management
plan are outputs of the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process. For instance, these
updates contain team responsibilities for stakeholder engagement activities that may need
to be updated.
- **B Project communications**
Incorrect. Project communications are inputs (not outputs) of the Monitor Stakeholder
Engagement process.
- **C Change management plan**
Incorrect. Although change requests are outputs of the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement
process, the change management plan is not an output.
- **D Presentations**
Incorrect. Presentations are a type of tool and technique used in this process. Presentations
are not outputs of the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process.

Question 123 of 210
Question ID: 651504
In which of the following processes could voting be used as a decision-making technique?
Top of Form
- **A Collect Requirements and Validate Scope**
- **B Plan Scope Management and Define Scope**
- **C Define Scope and Control Scope**
- **D Control Scope and Create WBS**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Remember the definition of each process to identify which processes may need to use
decision-making techniques such as voting.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Decision-making techniques is a team-based approach that useful for engaging stakeholders to
define their requirements for the project during the Collect Requirements process, as well as to
reach a decision on the validation method and who should perform the validation which is a part
of validating scope. The other processes listed in the question do not often use this technique.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Collect Requirements and Validate Scope**
Correct. Decision-making technique is used in the Collect Requirements process to
generate and prioritize project requirements by engaging the stakeholders and team
members in defining requirements. The Validate Scope process may also need to use the
decision-making technique in order to determine whether the validation is performed by the
team or others.

---

- **B Plan Scope Management and Define Scope**
Incorrect. The Plan Scope Management process often uses expert judgment and meetings to
develop the scope management plan while the project scope is often defined through a
workshop or using product analysis technique. These two processes do not usually need the
decision-making techniques such as voting.
- **C Define Scope and Control Scope**
Incorrect. The Control Scope process is to monitor the status of the scope by using the
variance analysis technique. It does not require the use of a decision-making technique
such as voting.
- **D Control Scope and Create WBS**
Incorrect. Both the Control Scope and Create WBS processes do not often use voting. While
the Control Scope process only needs to use the variance analysis to monitor the status of
the scope against the scope baseline, the Create WBS process mainly uses the
decomposition technique to subdivide the project into smaller components.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 689
Bottom of Form

Question 124 of 210
Question ID: 651601

---

The Acquire Resources process has eight outputs, including:
● Physical resource assignments
● Resource calendars
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project document updates
● EEF updates
● OPA updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
Top of Form
- **A Pre-assignment**
- **B Resource availability**
- **C Resource chain of custody documentation**
- **D Project team assignments**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Acquire Resources is the process of obtaining team members, facilities, equipment, materials,
supplies, and other resources necessary to complete project work. What would document such
acquisitions?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Acquire Resources is the process of obtaining team members, facilities, equipment, materials,
supplies, and other resources necessary to complete project work. The eight outputs of the
Acquire Resources process include:
● Physical resource assignments
● Project team assignments (a project team directory, organization chart, roles, and
responsibilities)
● Resource calendars
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project document updates

---

● EEF updates
● OPA updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Pre-assignment**
Incorrect. The physical or team resources may be determined in advance if specified in the
project charter, or if the project is dependent upon the expertise of particular persons.
However, pre-assignment is a tool for acquiring resources, not an output.
- **B Resource availability**
Incorrect. Resource availability is information provided by the resource calendars, which
serve as an output already listed in the question.
- **C Resource chain of custody documentation**
Incorrect. The chain of custody documentation for physical resources is not explicitly listed
as an output of the Acquire Resources process, nor any other process. This choice is merely
made up of legal and project management terms.
- **D Project team assignments**
Correct. The project team assignments are a principal output of the Acquire Resources
process, documenting the team members that have been acquired and their roles and
responsibilities for the project, in the form of a team directory, project organization chart,
and schedules.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 333-335
