Question 125 of 210
Question ID: 651614
Which of the following is an input to the Plan Communications Management process?
Top of Form
- **A Communications management plan**
- **B Project management plan**
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
- **D Communications requirement matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Plan Communications Management process includes determining the communication needs
of stakeholders and team members.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Plan Communications Management is the process of developing an appropriate approach and
plan for project communication activities based on the information needs of each stakeholder or
group, available organizational assets, and the needs of the project. The Plan Communications
Management process has the following five inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan is an output from the Plan
Communications Management process, not an input to the process.
- **B Project management plan**
Correct. The resource management and stakeholder engagement plans are two components
of the project management plan that contain communication information that can be used
as an input to the Plan Communications Management process.
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not include the requirements traceability matrix as an
input to the Plan Communications Management process.
- **D Communications requirement matrix**
Incorrect. Communications requirements matrix is a fake term made up for this question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 126 of 210
Question ID: 651674
Which of the following statements is correct about the Plan Schedule Management process?
Top of Form
- **A The process has two outputs: the schedule management plan and project documents updates.**
- **B The process has three outputs: the schedule management plan, project management plan**
updates, and project documents updates.
- **C The process has one output: the schedule management plan.**
- **D The process has two outputs: the schedule management plan and the schedule model**
development approach.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Plan Schedule Management process is one of the earlier processes in the project life cycle.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Plan Schedule Management process has only one output:
● Schedule management plan

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The process has two outputs: the schedule management plan and project documents**
updates.
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not list project documents updates among the outputs
of the Plan Schedule Management process.

---

- **B The process has three outputs: the schedule management plan, project management plan**
updates, and project documents updates.
Incorrect. Neither project management plan updates nor project documents updates are
listed in the PMBOK® Guide as outputs of the Plan Schedule Management process.
- **C The process has one output: the schedule management plan.**
Correct. The schedule management plan is the only output listed in the PMBOK® Guide
for the Plan Schedule Management process.
- **D The process has two outputs: the schedule management plan and the schedule model**
development approach.
Incorrect. The schedule model development approach specifies the scheduling methodology
and the scheduling tool to be used in the development of the project schedule model and is
typically included as part of the schedule management plan. Therefore, this answer is
incorrect.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 179, 181-182

Question 127 of 210
Question ID: 651654

---

The Plan Procurement Management process has ten outputs, including:
● Procurement management plan
● Procurement strategy
● Bid documents
● Procurement statement of work
● Source selection criteria
● Make-or-buy decisions
● Change requests
● Project documents updates
● Organizational process assets updates
Which of the following outputs is missing from the list?
Top of Form
- **A Risk report updates**
- **B Deliverables**
- **C Performance reports**
- **D Independent cost estimates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer may be useful when choosing a vendor.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Plan Procurement Management is the process of documenting project procurement decisions,
specifying the approach, and identifying potential sellers. The Plan Procurement Management
process has the following ten outputs:
● Procurement management plan
● Procurement strategy
● Bid documents
● Procurement statement of work
● Source selection criteria
● Make-or-buy decisions
● Independent cost estimates
● Change requests

---

● Project documents updates
● Organizational process assets updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk report updates**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide includes the risk register as a project document that might
be updated as a result of the Plan Procurement Management process but not the risk report.
- **B Deliverables**
Incorrect. Deliverables are not included in the list of the outputs of the Plan Procurement
Management process.
- **C Performance reports**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not explicitly list performance reports as an output of
the Plan Procurement Management process.
- **D Independent cost estimates**
Correct. The performing organization may decide to use an outside estimator to provide a
cost estimate that will be used as a benchmark on proposed vendor responses. Therefore,
independent cost estimates are outputs of the Plan Procurement Management process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 128 of 210
Question ID: 651569
Which of the following is not a tool or technique of the Estimate Activity Resources process?
Top of Form
- **A Expert judgment**
- **B Pre-assignment**
- **C Project management information system**
- **D Alternative analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

All the choices support the process of estimating the type and quantities of material, people,
equipment, or supplies required to perform each activity, while one precludes the need for an
estimate.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Estimate Activity Resources is the process of estimating team resources and the type and
quantities of material, equipment, and supplies necessary to perform project work. This process
has the following seven tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Bottom-up estimating
● Analogous estimating
● Parametric estimating
● Data analysis (alternative analysis)
● Project management information systems (PMIS)
● Meetings

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is explicitly listed as a tool for this process. Expertise should be
considered from individuals or groups with specialized knowledge or training in either
resource planning or estimating for both teams and physical resources.
- **B Pre-assignment**
Correct. The physical or team resources may be determined in advance if specified in the
project charter, or if the project is dependent upon the expertise of particular persons.
However, pre-assignment is a tool for the Acquire Resources process, not the Estimate
Activity Resources process.
- **C Project management information system**
Incorrect. A PMIS is explicitly listed as a tool for this process. Resource management
software can help plan, organize, and manage resource pools and develop resource
estimates, and possibly define the resource breakdown structures, resource availability,
resource rates, and resource calendars to assist in optimizing resource utilization.
- **D Alternative analysis**
Incorrect. Alternative analysis is explicitly listed as a data analysis technique for this
process, to select the best approach for completing the project activities. With alternative
analysis, you evaluate options including various levels of skill, different equipment
capacities, manual or automated tools, and make-rent-or-buy decisions.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 324-325, 333
Bottom of Form

Question 129 of 210
Question ID: 651558
Which of the following is not an output of the Control Scope process?
Top of Form
- **A Work performance data**
- **B Work performance information**
- **C Project documents updates**
- **D Change requests**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Control Scope is the process of monitoring the status of the project and product scope and
managing changes to the scope baseline.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Work performance data is not an output of Control Scope, but an input. The Control Scope
process has the following outputs: work performance information, change requests, project
management plan updates, and project document plan updates.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance data**

---

Correct. Work performance data is an output of the Direct and Manage Project Work
process during project execution. Such data does not serve as an output of Control Scope,
but an input.
- **B Work performance information**
Incorrect. Work performance information is a valid output of the Control Scope process,
resulting from analysis of work performance data about the number of change requests
received, the number of change requests accepted, and the number of deliverables verified,
validated, and completed.
- **C Project documents updates**
Incorrect. Updates to project documents such as the lessons learned register, requirements
documentation, and the requirements traceability matrix are valid outputs in controlling
scope.
- **D Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are valid outputs of the Control Scope process, which is
concerned with monitoring the status of the scope of the project and its deliverable
products. To manage changes to the scope, variance analysis may determine that change
requests for corrective or preventive actions are appropriate.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 170-171

Question 130 of 210
Question ID: 651565
Which of the following is not an input to the Sequence Activities process?
Top of Form
- **A Approved change requests**
- **B Activity list**
- **C Milestone list**
- **D Activity attributes**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Sequence Activities is in the Planning Process Group. Which of the answers would not typically
be an input to a planning process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Sequence Activities process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., activity list, activity attributes, milestone list)
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
The process is where the relationships among the project activities are identified and
documented.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Approved change requests**

---

Correct. Approved change requests are not listed as inputs to the Sequence Activities
process in the PMBOK® Guide. Therefore, this choice is the correct answer.
- **B Activity list**
Incorrect. The activity list contains all schedule activities required on the project that are to
be sequenced. The activity list is an example of one of the project documents that are inputs
to the Sequence Activities process.
- **C Milestone list**
Incorrect. The milestone list may have scheduled dates for specific milestones, which may
influence the way activities are sequenced and, therefore, is an input to the Sequence
Activities process. The milestone list is an example of a project document.
- **D Activity attributes**
Incorrect. Activity attributes may describe a necessary sequence of events or defined
predecessor or successor relationships, as well as defined lead and lag and logical
relationships between the activities. Activity attributes are an example of a project
document that is an input to the Sequence Activities process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 187, 188

Question 131 of 210
Question ID: 651506
Which of the following outputs corresponds to the appropriate process?
Top of Form
- **A Project charter: Plan Resource Management**
- **B Team performance assessments: Manage Team**
- **C Change requests: Develop Team**
- **D Resource requirements: Acquire Resources**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Read each choice carefully and think about the purpose of each process.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Change requests may result from the Manage Team process. In the Project Resource
Management Knowledge Area, change requests are also outputs of the Acquire Resources,
Develop Team, and Control Resources processes.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter: Plan Resource Management**
Incorrect. A project charter is an input (not an output) of the Plan Resource Management
process.
- **B Team performance assessments: Manage Team**
Incorrect. Team performance assessments are outputs of the Develop Team process but not
the Manage Team process.

---

- **C Change requests: Develop Team**
Correct. Change requests are outputs of the Develop Team process.
- **D Resource requirements: Acquire Resources**
Incorrect. Resource requirements are outputs of the Estimate Activity Resources process
(not the Acquire Resources process). The Acquire Resources process results in outputs such
as the physical resource assignments.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 308

Question 132 of 210
Question ID: 651535
Which of the following is typically not addressed as part of the roles and responsibilities in the
resource management plan?
Top of Form
- **A Assigned function**

---

- **B Authority**
- **C Compensation**
- **D Competence**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Part of the resource management plan provides guidance on roles and responsibilities which may
include team members’ required capacity and skill as well as decision-making privileges.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Plan Resource Management process has three outputs: the resource management plan, the
team charter, and project document updates. A major component of the resource management
plan is to provide guidance on resource roles and responsibilities, which typically cover four
items: role, authority, responsibility, and competency. Salary or compensation is part of cost
estimates for all resources but falls in the Project Cost Management Knowledge Area.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Assigned function**
Incorrect. A role is a team member’s assigned function in the project (such as civil
engineer, business analyst, and testing coordinator), and should be among the
documentation of roles and responsibilities in the resource management plan.
- **B Authority**
Incorrect. A team member’s authority may include the rights to apply project resources,
make decisions, sign approvals, accept deliverables and influence others to carry out the
work of the project, and is indeed included among the documentation of roles and
responsibilities in the resource management plan.
- **C Compensation**
Correct. Compensation or salary is not explicitly listed as part of the roles and
responsibilities described in the resource management plan. Instead, the cost estimated for

---

resources to perform the activities required for each work package is connected via
organizational procedure links in the WBS.
- **D Competence**
- **A team member’s competence is the skill and capacity required to complete assigned**
activities within the project constraints to achieve the desired project performance.
Competence is certainly included among the documentation of roles and responsibilities in
the resource management plan.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 318-319

Question 133 of 210
Question ID: 651664
Which of the following is a tool or technique used in the Develop Project Management Plan
process?
Top of Form
- **A Data analysis**

---

- **B Decision making**
- **C Interviews**
- **D Document analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Specific information needs to be obtained from stakeholders to develop the project management
plan.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Develop Project Management Plan has the following four tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering (e.g., interviews)
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Meetings
Develop Project Management Plan is the process of defining, preparing, and coordinating all
plan components and consolidating them into an integrated project management plan.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Data analysis**
Incorrect. Data analysis techniques are used to organize, assess, and evaluate data and
information. Data analysis is not a tool or technique used in the Develop Project
Management Plan process.
- **B Decision making**
Incorrect. Decision-making techniques are used to select a course of action from different
alternatives. The Develop Project Management Plan process does not use the
decision-making tool and technique.
- **C Interviews**

---

Correct. Interviews are an example of data-gathering techniques where a formal or
informal approach is used to elicit information from stakeholders by talking to them
directly. Interviews is a tool and technique used in the Develop Project Management Plan
process.
- **D Document analysis**
Incorrect. Document analysis is an example of the data analysis tool and technique.
Document analysis is not used during the Develop Project Management Plan process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 82, 85

Question 134 of 210
Question ID: 651572
Which of the following is an input to the Develop Schedule process?
Top of Form
- **A Agreements**
- **B Project schedule**

---

- **C Issue log**
- **D Schedule network analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Many different aspects need to be considered when developing the project schedule such as the
availability of both physical and human resources, as well as any contracts with vendors.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Develop Schedule process is defined as "the process of analyzing activity sequences,
durations, resource requirements, and schedule constraints to create the project schedule model
for project execution and monitoring and controlling". The Develop Schedule process has the
following five inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents
● Agreements
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Agreements**
Correct. Vendors may influence the project schedule as they develop the details of how they
will perform the project work to meet contractual commitments. Therefore, agreements are
inputs to the Develop Schedule process.
- **B Project schedule**
Incorrect. The project schedule is an output (not an input) of the Develop Schedule process
that presents linked activities with planned dates, durations, milestones, and resources.
- **C Issue log**
Incorrect. The issue log is a project document where information about issues is recorded
and monitored. While several project documents are inputs to the Develop Schedule
process, the PMBOK® Guide does not list the issue log as one of these project documents.

---

- **D Schedule network analysis**
Incorrect. Schedule network analysis is the overarching technique used to generate the
project schedule model. Therefore, schedule network analysis is a tool and technique used
in the Develop Schedule process, not an input to the process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 205, 208

Question 135 of 210
Question ID: 651530
Which of the following is not an input to the Control Schedule process?
Top of Form
- **A The status of activities**
- **B Project calendars**
- **C Scheduling software**

---

- **D Monitoring and reporting methods to be used**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is an example of an input common to the majority of processes but is not an
input to the Control Schedule process.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Control Schedule process is where the status of the project is monitored to update the project
schedule and manage changes to the schedule baseline. The process has the following four
inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., project calendars)
● Work performance data (e.g., the status of activities)
● Organizational process assets (e.g., monitoring and reporting methods to be used)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The status of activities**
Incorrect. The status of activities is included in work performance data which is an input to
the Control Schedule process.
- **B Project calendars**
Incorrect. A project calendar identifies working days and shifts that are available for
scheduled activities. A schedule model may require more than one project calendar to allow
for different work periods for some activities. Project calendars are an example of a project
document that is an input to the Control Schedule process.
- **C Scheduling software**
Correct. Scheduling software is an example of an enterprise environmental factor, which is
not listed as an input to the Control Schedule process in the PMBOK® Guide.
- **D Monitoring and reporting methods to be used**

---

Incorrect. Monitoring and reporting methods to be used in the Control Schedule process
are an example of organizational process assets, which are inputs to the process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 222, 225

Question 136 of 210
Question ID: 651679
When first gathering the project information to be considered as part of collecting requirements,
which of the following might be left undone until after the requisite items are gathered?
Top of Form
- **A Project business case**
- **B Agreements**
- **C Stakeholder engagement plan**
- **D Affinity diagram**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Collect Requirements has seven inputs. One of the choices may be a tool, technique, or output
that can be left undone until after you have collected the inputs.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Collect Requirements is the process of determining, documenting, and managing stakeholder
needs and requirements to meet project objectives. This process has these seven inputs, some of
which have multiple components:
● Project charter
● Project management plan (scope management plan, requirements management plan,
stakeholder engagement plan)
● Project documents (assumption log, lessons learned register, stakeholder register)
● Business documents (business case)
● Agreements
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets
Of the choices, the affinity diagram is not listed among the inputs because it is a data analysis
technique that would be performed after inputs are gathered.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project business case**
Incorrect. The project business case may describe the required, desired, and optional
criteria for meeting the business needs and therefore serves as an input business document
for the Collect Requirements process.
- **B Agreements**
Incorrect. Agreements with suppliers may contain project and product requirements and
therefore serve as inputs to the Collect Requirements process.
- **C Stakeholder engagement plan**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement plan is a component of the project management
plan that is explicitly listed as an input to the Collect Requirements process, due to the need
to understand stakeholder communication requirements and the level of stakeholder

---

engagement, and in turn assess and adapt to the level of participation in requirements
collection activities.
- **D Affinity diagram**
Correct. The affinity diagram does not serve as an input but is instead a tool and technique
for the Collect Requirements process. This data representation technique allows large
numbers of ideas that have been brainstormed about requirements to be classified into
groups for review and analysis.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 140-141

Question ID: 651616
Which of the following is an output of the Plan Communications Management process?
Top of Form
- **A Project document updates**
- **B Risk register updates**

---

- **C Change requests**
- **D Project communications**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

As a result of carrying out the Plan Communications Management process, other documents may
need changes.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Plan Communications Management process has the following three outputs:
● Communications management plan
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
Plan Communications Management is the process of developing an appropriate approach and
plan for project communication activities based on the information needs of each stakeholder or
group, available organizational assets, and the needs of the project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project document updates**
Correct. The project schedule and the stakeholder register are two project documents that
might be updated as a result of the Plan Communications Management process. Therefore,
project documents updates are outputs of the process.
- **B Risk register updates**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not include risk register updates among the outputs of
the Plan Communications Management process.
- **C Change requests**
Incorrect. Change requests are not an output from the Plan Communications Management
process and are typically not outputs of any of the processes where management plans are
developed.

---

- **D Project communications**

the Plan Communications Management process.

Question 138 of 210
Question ID: 651592
Which of the following is not an output of the Manage Quality process?
Top of Form
- **A Scope baseline updates**
- **B Quality control measurements**
- **C Issue log updates**

---

- **D Change requests**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Manage Quality process uses the measurements gathered during the Control Quality process
to determine if the work is the right quality.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Manage Quality is the process of translating the quality management plan into executable quality
activities that incorporate the organization's quality policies into the project. The Manage Quality
process has the following five outputs:
● Quality reports
● Test and evaluation documents
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates (e.g., scope baseline)
● Project documents updates (e.g., issue log)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Scope baseline updates**
Incorrect. As part of the project management plan updates that are outputs of the Manage
Quality process, the scope baseline may change as a result of specific quality management
activities. Therefore, scope baseline updates are outputs of the process.
- **B Quality control measurements**
Correct. Quality control measurements are inputs to the Manage Quality process, not an
output. Therefore, this choice is the correct answer to the question asked.
- **C Issue log updates**
Incorrect. New issues raised as a result of the Manage Quality process are recorded in the
issue log. The issue log is one example of the project documents updates that are outputs of
the Manage Quality process.
- **D Change requests**

---

Incorrect. Any changes that occur during the Manage Quality process that impact any of
the documents under configuration control require following the organization's change
control policy, which typically begins with a change request. Therefore, change requests are
outputs of the Manage Quality process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 288, 296-297

Question 139 of 210
Question ID: 651678
Which of the following is not a component of the scope management plan?
Top of Form
- **A A process that enables the creation of the WBS from the detailed project scope statement**
- **B A process that establishes how the scope baseline will be approved and maintained**
- **C A tracking structure that reflects the attributes to be captured on a requirements traceability**
matrix

---

- **D A method for obtaining stakeholders' formal acceptance of the completed project deliverables**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Plan Scope Management process has two output components of the project management
plan. Which of these choices would belong to another component that is not the scope
management plan?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scope management plan is a component of the project management plan that describes how
the scope will be defined, developed, monitored, controlled and validated. The scope
management plan's components include a process for preparing a project scope statement as well
as what is listed in the choices. The exception is a traceability structure that reflects the
requirement attributes captured on the traceability matrix, which is a component of the
requirements management plan, also known as the business analysis plan, the purpose of which
is to describe how the project and product requirements will be analyzed, documented, and
managed.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A A process that enables the creation of the WBS from the detailed project scope statement**
Incorrect. This choice describes a valid component of the scope management plan.
- **B A process that establishes how the scope baseline will be approved and maintained**
Incorrect. This choice describes a valid component of the scope management plan.
- **C A tracking structure that reflects the attributes to be captured on a requirements**
traceability matrix
Correct. This choice describes a component of the requirements management plan, which is
an output of the Plan Scope Management process but is distinct from the scope
management plan.
- **D A method for obtaining stakeholders' formal acceptance of the completed project**
deliverables
Incorrect. This choice describes a valid component of the scope management plan.

---

Question 140 of 210
Question ID: 651588
Which of the following is not a tool or technique of the Plan Quality Management process?
Top of Form
- **A Quality metrics**
- **B Interviews**
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
- **D Mind mapping**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

During the Plan Quality Management process, information is collected, and decisions are made
on how the project will handle quality.

---

Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Plan Quality Management process has the following seven tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering (e.g., interviews)
● Data analysis (e.g., cost-benefit analysis)
● Decision making
● Data representation (e.g., mind mapping)
● Test and inspection planning
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Quality metrics**
Correct. A quality metric specifically describes a project or product attribute and how the
Control Quality process will verify compliance to it. Quality metrics are outputs from the
Plan Quality Management process.
- **B Interviews**
Incorrect. Project and product quality needs and expectations can be identified by
interviewing experienced project participants, stakeholders, and subject matter experts.
Interviews are an example of the data-gathering tool and technique used in the Plan
Quality Management process.
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
Incorrect. Cost-benefit analysis is part of the data analysis tools and techniques used
during the Plan Quality Management process. A cost-benefit analysis will help the project
manager determine if the planned quality activities are cost-effective.
- **D Mind mapping**
Incorrect. Mind mapping is a diagrammatic method used to organize information visually
and can be useful in the rapid gathering of project quality requirements, constraints,
dependencies, and relationships. Data representation, of which mind mapping is an
example, is a tool and technique used in the Plan Quality Management process.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 277, 281-284

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 141 of 210
Question ID: 626027
As part of your communication strategy, you plan to create a website to share information with
the project stakeholders.
What type of communication method is this?
Top of Form
- **A Interactive communication**
- **B Pull communication**
- **C Push communication**
- **D Open communication**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

Which of the communications methods is best suited for large volumes of information and/or
large audiences?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

There are three main communication methods to share information among stakeholders: push
communication, pull communication, and interactive communication. Those methods are among
the tools and techniques that can be used as part of the Plan Communications Management
process implied by the scenario. Pull communication is often used for a mass communication
where the recipients may access the content at their discretion, often subject to security
procedures. Note, the pull method does not guarantee that the recipients are aware when or if
they need to access the information that has been published.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Interactive communication**
Incorrect. Interactive communication occurs between two or more parties performing a
multidirectional exchange of information. Example include meetings, phone calls, instant
messaging, and video conferencing. Websites are not considered an interactive
communication method.
- **B Pull communication**
Correct. Websites are an example of pull communication methods. Of the choices provided,
pull communication is the best answer to the question asked.
- **C Push communication**
Incorrect. Push communication is sent to specific recipients who need to receive the
information. Push communications include letters, memos, reports, emails, faxes, voice
mails, blogs, and press releases, but not websites.
- **D Open communication**
Incorrect. 'Open communication' is not specified in the PMBOK® Guide as a
communication method.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 374
Bottom of Form

Question 142 of 210
Question ID: 651598
Which of the following is an input to the Control Quality process?
Top of Form
- **A Change requests**
- **B Accepted deliverables**
- **C Quality control measurements**
- **D Quality metrics**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Control Quality process is performed to measure the completeness and compliance of a
product or service.
Correct Answer: D

---


**Explanation:**

Control Quality is the process of monitoring and recording results of executing the quality
management activities to assess performance and ensure the project outputs are complete,
correct, and meet customer expectations. The Control Quality process has the following seven
inputs:
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., quality metrics)
● Approved change requests
● Deliverables
● Work performance data
● Enterprise environmental factors
● Organizational process assets

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change requests**
Incorrect. 'Approved' change requests are inputs to the Control Quality process. However,
change requests are outputs from, not inputs to, the process.
- **B Accepted deliverables**
Incorrect. Accepted deliverables are deliverables that have been inspected and approved by
the customer and are outputs of the Validate Scope process. The Control Quality process
has deliverables as inputs and verified deliverables as outputs.
- **C Quality control measurements**
Incorrect. Quality control measurements are outputs from the Control Quality process, not
inputs to the process.
- **D Quality metrics**
Correct. Quality metrics describe which project or product attributes the Control Quality
process will measure and what will be considered compliant. Therefore, quality metrics are
inputs to the process, making this the correct answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 298, 300

---

Question 143 of 210
Question ID: 651584
The Control Costs process includes the following tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Earned value analysis (EVM)
● Variance analysis
● Reserve analysis
● Trend analysis
● To-complete performance index (TCPI)
Which of the following tools and techniques should be added to this list?
Top of Form
- **A Change control meetings**
- **B Forecasting**
- **C Project management information system**
- **D Bottom-up estimating**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Control Costs process is used to monitor the status of the project to update the project
budget and managing changes to the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Control Costs is the process of monitoring the status of the project to update the project costs and
manage changes to the cost baseline. This process has the following tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Earned value analysis (EVM)
● Variance analysis
● Reserve analysis
● Trend analysis
● To-complete performance index (TCPI)
● Project management information systems

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change control meetings**
Incorrect. Change control meetings are a type of meeting in the Perform Integrated Change
Control process. It is not used in the Control Costs process.
- **B Forecasting**
Incorrect. Although some tools and techniques can help in forecasting (i.e., to-complete
performance index (TCPI), estimate at complete (EAC), etc.) there is not a specific tool or
technique called forecasting.
- **C Project management information system**
Correct. Project management information systems are often used to monitor the three EVM
dimensions (PV, EV, and AC), to display graphical trends, and to forecast a range of
possible final project results.
- **D Bottom-up estimating**
Incorrect. Bottom-up estimating is a tool and technique in the Estimate Costs process. It is
not used in the Control Costs process.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 268

Question 144 of 210
Question ID: 651627
Which of the following is both an input and an output of the Plan Risk Responses process?
Top of Form
- **A Schedule baseline**
- **B Resource calendars**
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
- **D Risk register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is perhaps the most basic option.

---

Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The risk register is used heavily in all of the risk management processes. As an input to the Plan
Risk Responses process, it provides the list of all identified and prioritized individual risks that
may require response planning. As an output, the risk register will be updated with the agreed
upon risk responses, trigger conditions, and other related information.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule baseline**
Incorrect. The schedule baseline is an output but not an input of the Plan Risk Responses
process.
- **B Resource calendars**
Incorrect. Resource calendars are an input but not an output of the Plan Risk Responses
process.
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
Incorrect. Cost-benefit analysis is a tool and technique of the Plan Risk Responses process,
not an input or output.
- **D Risk register**
Correct. The risk register is both an input and an output of the Plan Risk Responses
process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 145 of 210
Question ID: 651689
Which of the following inputs to the Plan Cost Management process provides preapproved
financial resources?
Top of Form
- **A Organizational process assets**
- **B Project management plan**
- **C Project charter**
- **D Enterprise environmental factors**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The key word in the question is 'preapproved'.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project charter provides the preapproved financial resources from which the detailed project
costs are developed. It documents the initial parameters for the project. The project charter also
defines the project approval requirements that will influence the management of the project
costs.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Although organizational process assets or OPAs are inputs to the Plan Cost
Management process, they do not provide preapproved financial resources. Even though
money is a company asset, it is not a process. Funding is never provided through an OPA.
- **B Project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan, which includes the cost management plan,
describes how the funding will be used. The cost management plan is an output of the
process.
- **C Project charter**
Correct. The project charter provides the preapproved financial resources from which the
detailed project costs are developed. The project charter also defines the project approval
requirements that will influence the management of the project costs.
- **D Enterprise environmental factors**
Incorrect. Although enterprise environmental factors or EEFs are inputs to the Plan Cost
Management process, they do not provide preapproved financial resources. EEFs do not
include financial resources, but may indicate financial constraints such as legal spending
limits.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 236

Question 146 of 210
Question ID: 651509
Which of the following processes does not use the risk register as an input?
Top of Form
- **A Estimate Activity Resources**
- **B Plan Risk Management**
- **C Determine Budget**
- **D Plan Quality Management**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of when you use it as an input vs. output.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

This question can be tricky, If you don't read it carefully, at first, you might think that the risk
register would be used in the only process that is part of the Risk Management Knowledge Area,
but you should differentiate between inputs and outputs. The risk register is not an input of the
Plan Risk Management process. The risk register is created by the Identify Risks process and is
thus an output. It is then used extensively as an input in all the remaining risk management
processes and the other knowledge areas.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Estimate Activity Resources**
Incorrect. The risk register is an input to the Estimate Activity Resources process because it
describes the risks that can impact resource selection and availability.

---

- **B Plan Risk Management**
Correct. The risk register is not an input to the Plan Risk Management process but is
initially developed in the Identify Risks process.
- **C Determine Budget**
Incorrect. The risk register is an input to the Determine Budget process because the
register is reviewed to consider how to aggregate the risk response costs.
- **D Plan Quality Management**
Incorrect. The risk register is an input to the Plan Quality Management process because the
risk register contains information on threats and opportunities that may impact quality
requirements.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 396

Question 148 of 210
Question ID: 651516
What output of the Perform Integrated Change Control process serves as an input to both the
Control Quality and Control Procurements processes?
Top of Form
- **A Approved change requests**

---

- **B Change log**
- **C Project management plan updates**
- **D Project documents updates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What would typically be considered the primary output of the Perform Integrated Change
Control process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Perform Integrated Change Control Process is where all change requests are reviewed. It
also involves approving changes and managing changes to deliverables, organizational process
assets, project documents, and the project management plan; and communicating the decisions.
This process has the following three outputs:
● Approved change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project document updates (e.g., change log)
Project management plan updates and project document updates are not inputs to any process.
Therefore, 'approved change requests' is the only viable answer.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Approved change requests**
Correct. Approved change requests such as defect repairs or revised work methods could
affect the Control Quality process, whereas, approved change requests such as
modifications to the contract or the procurement statement of work would affect the Control
Procurements. Approved change requests are also inputs to the Direct and Manage Project
Work process.
- **B Change log**

---

Incorrect. While the change log is an output from the Perform Integrated Change Control
process as a project document update, it is not an input to the Control Quality or Control
Procurements processes.
- **C Project management plan updates**
Incorrect. Project management plan updates are outputs from, not inputs to, the Control
Quality and Control Procurement processes.
- **D Project documents updates**
Incorrect. Project documents updates are outputs from, not inputs to, the Control Quality
and Control Procurement processes.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 113-114, 120

Question 149 of 210
Question ID: 651647
Which tool and technique used during the Implement Risk Responses process helps the project
manager to encourage nominated risk owners to take necessary action where required?
Top of Form

---

- **A Data gathering**
- **B Influencing**
- **C Expert judgment**
- **D Project management information system**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of the purpose of each tool or technique and whether it helps to move people to action.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Implement Risk Responses is the process of implementing agreed-upon risk response plans. This
process includes the following three tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Interpersonal and team skills (e.g., influencing)
● Project management information system

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Data gathering**
Incorrect. Although data gathering tools such as brainstorming, checklists, and interviews
are used in most of the risk management processes, these tools are not employed during the
Implement Risk Responses process.
- **B Influencing**
Correct. Influencing is a tool and technique employed during the Implement Risk
Responses process to help the project manager encourage nominated risk owners to take
necessary action where required.
- **C Expert judgment**

---

Incorrect. Expert judgment facilitates the consideration of expertise from individuals or
groups with specialized knowledge to validate or modify risk responses and decide how to
implement them in the most efficient and effective manner. It is not specifically about
encouraging nominated risk owners to take necessary action where required.
- **D Project management information system**
Incorrect. Project management information systems or PMIS can include schedule,
resource, and cost modules to ensure that agreed-upon risk response plans and their
associated activities are fully integrated into the project. PMIS does not correspond to what
is described in the question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 449, 451

Question 150 of 210
Question ID: 651520
The sponsor asks the project manager if the software the project has developed so far conforms
to all the requirements.
What should be used to measure completion of the product scope?
Top of Form

---

- **A Requirements documentation**
- **B Project management plan**
- **C WBS**
- **D Accepted deliverables**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of which item contains the specifications for the product.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

This scenario indicates you are conducting the Validate Scope process to measure completion of
the product scope. Remember, completion of the project scope is measured against the
components of the project management plan, namely the scope baseline. Completion of the
product scope is measured against a project document, namely the product requirements
documentation, making “requirements documentation” the best choice to answer the question.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements documentation**
Correct. Completion of the product scope is measured against the product requirements
documentation, which serves as an input to the Validate Scope process.
- **B Project management plan**
Incorrect. Completion of the project scope is measured against the project management
plan. Although the project management plan includes the project scope baseline, this
question requires a more specific answer.
- **C WBS**
Incorrect. The WBS contains a subdivision of project deliverables and project work into
smaller, more manageable components. However, since the WBS does not contain details of

---

how the deliverables will measurably fulfill the requirements, this choice is not the best
answer.
- **D Accepted deliverables**
Incorrect. Accepted deliverables are outputs of the Validate Scope process and then serve
as an input to the Close Project or Phase process. In this scenario, the project manager is
still in the process of validating scope and needs to compare verified deliverables (from the
Control Quality process) to another input of the Validate Scope process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 131, 165

Question 151 of 210
Question ID: 651638
Which of the following is not an input to the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process?
Top of Form
- **A Risk register**
- **B Influence diagrams**

---

- **C Scope baseline**
- **D Risk management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which choice is a tool or technique rather than an input?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis is the process of numerically analyzing the effect of
identified individual project risks and other sources of uncertainty on overall project objectives.
The process has the following four inputs:
● Project management plan (including the risk management plan and the schedule baseline)
● Project documents (including the risk register)
● Organizational process assets
● Enterprise environmental factors

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is an input of the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process,
where it provides the details of individual project risks used as the basis for overall project
risk.
- **B Influence diagrams**
Correct. Influence diagrams are not an input of the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis
process - instead, they are a graphical data analysis technique used during this process to
aid decision making under uncertainty.
- **C Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The scope baseline is an input of the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process,
where it describes the starting point from which the effect of individual project risks and
other sources of uncertainty are evaluated.

---

- **D Risk management plan**
Incorrect. The risk management plan is an input of the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis
process. It specifies whether quantitative analysis is required for the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 428, 436

Question 152 of 210
Question ID: 651502
Which of the following outputs from the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group flow to the
Closing Process Group?
Top of Form
- **A Project charter**
- **B Accepted deliverables**
- **C Approved change requests**

---

- **D Deliverables**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

First, consider which choice is a result of monitoring and controlling activities. Of the two valid
choices, consider which becomes an input to the Close Project or Phase process.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Accepted deliverables are the products, results, or capability to perform a service that is
produced by a project. Each deliverable becomes validated as meeting the specified acceptance
criteria as an output of the Validate Scope process. Approved product specifications, delivery
receipts, and work performance documents acknowledge the formal stakeholder acceptance of
the project's deliverables, which are then used in the Close Project or Phase process to produce
the final transition and report.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter**
Incorrect. A project charter is used in the Planning Process Group after it is developed in
the Initiating Process Group.
- **B Accepted deliverables**
Correct. Accepted deliverables flow from Validate Scope in the Monitoring and Controlling
Process Group to the Closing Process Group.
- **C Approved change requests**
Incorrect. Approved change requests are created in the Monitoring and Controlling Process
Group and then used in the Executing Process Group.
- **D Deliverables**
Incorrect. Note that 'accepted deliverables' differ from 'deliverables'. Deliverables are
created in the Executing Process Group and are then used in the Monitoring and
Controlling Process Group.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166, 125

Question 153 of 210
Question ID: 651552
The Collect Requirements process has two outputs, including requirements documentation.
Which is the other output?
Top of Form
- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
- **B Project schedule network diagrams**
- **C Project management plan**
- **D Work performance information**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Collect Requirements is the process of defining and documenting stakeholders' needs to meet the
project objectives.

---

Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Collect Requirements is the process of determining, documenting, and managing stakeholder
needs and requirements to meet project objectives. The Collect Requirements process has the
following two outputs:
● Requirements documentation
● Requirements traceability matrix

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Requirements traceability matrix**
Correct. The other output is the requirements traceability matrix, a grid that provides a way
to track requirements throughout the project life cycle, linking each requirement to the
business and project objectives that make the requirements valuable and provide a structure
for managing changes to the product scope.
- **B Project schedule network diagrams**
Incorrect. The project schedule network diagrams are outputs for the Sequence Activities
and Develop Schedule processes.
- **C Project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan serves as an input for all processes in the Scope
Management Knowledge Area.
- **D Work performance information**
Incorrect. Work performance information can only result from the analysis that takes place
in the processes that belong in the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group. Of the
Project Scope Management processes, only the Validate Scope and Control Scope processes
generate work performance information. Remember, the Collect Requirements process is in
the Planning Process Group.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 138, 148-149
Bottom of Form

Question 154 of 210
Question ID: 651597
Which of the following is not a tool and technique of the Control Quality process?
Top of Form
- **A Scatter diagrams**
- **B Histograms**
- **C Context diagrams**
- **D Questionnaires and surveys**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Control Quality process involves collecting, analyzing, and depicting data to assess the
quality of the deliverables.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Control Quality process has the following six tools and techniques:

---

● Data gathering (e.g., questionnaires and surveys)
● Data analysis
● Inspection
● Testing/product evaluations
● Data representation (e.g., histograms, scatter diagrams)
● Meetings
Control Quality is the process of monitoring and recording results of executing the quality
management activities to assess performance and ensure the project outputs are complete,
correct, and meet customer expectations.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Scatter diagrams**
Incorrect. Scatter diagrams are a type of data representation technique that can be used as
a tool and technique in the Control Quality process.
- **B Histograms**
Incorrect. Histograms are a type of data representation technique that can be used as a tool
and technique in the Control Quality process.
- **C Context diagrams**
Correct. A context diagram can be used to depict the product scope of a project visually
and is a tool and technique of the Collect Requirements process. The PMBOK® Guide does
not include context diagrams as a tool or technique used in the Control Quality process;
therefore, this choice is the correct answer.
- **D Questionnaires and surveys**
Incorrect. Questionnaires and surveys are types of data gathering techniques that can be
used as a tool and technique in the Control Quality process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 298, 146

PMP Exam 8 (ITTO)
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 155 of 210
Question ID: 651641
Which of the choices below is an input of the Implement Risk Responses process?
Top of Form
- **A Risk report updates**
- **B Lessons learned register updates**
- **C Risk register updates**
- **D Risk management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which option provides guidance to the process?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Implement Risk Responses is the process of implementing agreed-upon risk response plans. This
process has the following three inputs:
● Project management plan (e.g., the risk management plan)
● Project documents (including the lessons learned register, the risk register, and the risk report)

---

● Organizational process assets
The process has two outputs:
● Change requests
● Project documents updates (including the issue log, the lessons learned register, project team
assignments, the risk register, and the risk report)

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk report updates**
Incorrect. The risk report is an input of the process (where it provides an assessment of the
current overall project risk exposure as well as the agreed upon risk response strategy),
and risk report updates is an output, (where it is updated to reflect any changes made).
- **B Lessons learned register updates**
Incorrect. While the lessons learned register is an input of the Implement Risk Responses
process (where it provides lessons learned earlier in the project concerning risk responses),
and lessons learned register updates is an output (where it is updated with information on
challenges encountered and approaches that worked well).
- **C Risk register updates**
Incorrect. While the risk register is an input of the Implement Risk Responses process
(where it provides the agreed-upon risk responses and the nominated owners), and risk
register updates is an output (where the register is updated to reflect any changes to the
agreed-upon responses).
- **D Risk management plan**
Correct. The risk management plan is an input of the Implement Risk Responses process.
The risk management plan provides roles and responsibilities for risk management, the
level of detail for the risk management methodology, and the project's risk thresholds.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 449
Bottom of Form

Question 156 of 210
Question ID: 651658
Which of the following is an output of the Control Procurements process?
Top of Form
- **A Work performance reports**
- **B Enterprise environmental factors updates**
- **C Closed procurements**
- **D Audit reports**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is required regarding procurements before the project can be closed?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Conduct Procurements is the process of obtaining seller responses, selecting a seller, and
awarding a contract. The Control Procurements process has the following seven outputs:
● Closed procurements
● Work performance information

---

● Procurement documentation updates
● Change requests
● Project management plan updates
● Project documents updates
● Organizational process assets updates

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Work performance reports**
Incorrect. Work performance reports are outputs of the Monitor and Control Project Work
process, not the Control Procurements process,
- **B Enterprise environmental factors updates**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does not include enterprise environmental factors updates
as an output from the Control Procurements process.
- **C Closed procurements**
Correct. Closing procurements consist of tying up all the loose ends of procurement,
verifying all work and deliverables are accepted, finalizing open claims, and providing the
seller with formal written notice that the contract has been completed. Closed
procurements are the outputs of the Control Procurements process.
- **D Audit reports**
Incorrect. The results of audits would be work performance data which would be analyzed
in context to become work performance information. Audit reports are not a term used in
the PMBOK® Guide.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 492, 499

Question 157 of 210
Question ID: 651691
Which input to the Plan Cost Management process provides the approach for identifying,
analyzing, and monitoring unexpected events on the project?
Top of Form
- **A Schedule management plan**
- **B Risk management plan**
- **C Organizational process assets**
- **D Project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Estimation is always coupled with another aspect of project management.?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The inputs to the cost management plan are the project charter, the project management plan
(primarily the schedule and risk management plan), enterprise environmental factors, and
organizational process assets. The risk management plan provides an approach for identifying,
analyzing, and monitoring risks. The risk management plan provides processes and controls that
will impact cost estimation and management.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule management plan**
Incorrect. The schedule management plan establishes the criteria and the activities for
developing, monitoring, and controlling the schedule. It is not used to determine the
approach for identifying, analyzing, and monitoring unexpected events on the project.
- **B Risk management plan**
Correct. The risk management plan provides an approach for identifying, analyzing, and
monitoring unexpected events (risks).
- **C Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. OPAs, which are useful for the Plan Cost Management process include financial
controls procedures, historical information, lessons learned repository, financial databases,
existing formal and informal cost estimating, and budgeting-related policies, procedures,
and guidelines. These OPAs are not specifically used in this process to determine the
approach for identifying, analyzing, and monitoring unexpected events on the project.
- **D Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter provides the preapproved financial resources from which the
detailed project costs are developed. The project charter also defines the project approval
requirements that will influence the management of the project costs. The project charter is
not specifically used in this process to determine the approach for identifying, analyzing,
and monitoring unexpected events on the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 236

Question 158 of 210
Question ID: 651513
Which tool or technique used during the Plan Risk Responses process specifies that expertise
should be considered from individuals or groups with specialized knowledge in threat response
strategies, opportunity response strategies, contingent response strategies, and overall project risk
response strategies?
Top of Form
- **A Expert judgment**
- **B Multicriteria decision analysis**
- **C Alternative analysis**
- **D Project team assignments**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct choice is all about expertise.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Plan Risk Responses is the process of developing options, selecting strategies, and agreeing on
actions to address overall project risk exposure, as well as to treat individual project risks. This
process employs nine tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering
● Interpersonal and team skills
● Strategies for threats
● Strategies for opportunities

---

● Contingent response strategies
● Strategies for overall project risk
● Data analysis
● Decision making

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Expert judgment**
Correct. Expert judgment dictates that expertise should be considered from individuals or
groups with specialized knowledge in threat response strategies, opportunity response
strategies, contingent response strategies, and overall project risk response strategies, as
well as individuals with particular expertise relevant to specific project risks.
- **B Multicriteria decision analysis**
Incorrect. Multicriteria decision analysis is a decision-making technique that is used
during the Plan Risk Responses process. It utilizes a decision matrix to provide a systematic
approach to establishing key decision criteria, evaluating and ranking alternatives, and
selecting a preferred option.
- **C Alternative analysis**
Incorrect. Alternative analysis is a data analysis technique used in the Plan Risk Responses
process. It involves simple comparisons of the characteristics and requirements of
alternative risk response options.
- **D Project team assignments**
Incorrect. Project team assignments is not a tool or technique but is instead an input and
output of the Plan Risk Responses process that allocates the necessary resources to each
risk response action, including suitably qualified and experienced personnel.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 437, 441
Bottom of Form

Question 159 of 210
Question ID: 651693
Which of the following is not a tool and technique of the Identify Stakeholders process?
Top of Form
- **A Questionnaires and surveys**
- **B Document analysis**
- **C Meetings**
- **D Process analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer has the least relevance to stakeholder identification?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Identify Stakeholders is the process of identifying project stakeholders regularly and analyzing
and documenting relevant information regarding their interests, involvement, interdependencies,
influence, and potential impact on project success. The Identify Stakeholders process has five
tools and techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Data gathering (e.g., questionnaires and surveys)
● Data analysis (e.g., document analysis)

---

● Data representation
● Meetings

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Questionnaires and surveys**
Incorrect. Questionnaires and surveys are a data gathering technique used during the
Identify Stakeholder process to collect stakeholder information.
- **B Document analysis**
Incorrect. Document analysis is used during the Identify Stakeholder process to assess the
available project documentation and lessons learned from previous projects.
- **C Meetings**
Incorrect. Meetings are employed during the Identify Stakeholders process to develop an
understanding of significant project stakeholders.
- **D Process analysis**
Correct. Although process analysis is a technique used in project quality management, it is
not used during the Identify Stakeholders process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 507

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 160 of 210
Question ID: 651528
What process should be performed first as part of project planning, and what tool or technique
can be used?
Top of Form
- **A Collect Requirements using expert judgment**
- **B Plan Scope Management using alternatives analysis**
- **C Create WBS using decomposition**
- **D Define Scope using interpersonal and team skills**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think of which process the project manager might first undertake in the Planning Process Group
as part of the Project Scope Management Knowledge Area, and which tool would be helpful for
that process.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

While Develop Project Management Plan is listed as the first process in the Planning Process
Group, this process serves as an umbrella for the development of the subsidiary plans. Project
planning typically starts with the development of the scope management plan. In other words,
Plan Scope Management is essentially the first process that is carried out as part of project
planning. A data analysis technique that can be used for this process includes but is not limited to
alternatives analysis. This analysis covers the rest of the Project Scope Management Knowledge
Area processes, such as the evaluation of various ways of collecting requirements, elaborating
the project and product scope, creating the product, validating the scope, and controlling the
scope.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Collect Requirements using expert judgment**
Incorrect. While expert judgment is one of the tools and techniques used in the Collect
Requirements process, a scope management plan must be in place before starting the
process of collecting requirements.
- **B Plan Scope Management using alternatives analysis**
Correct. Plan Scope Management is the first planning process which results in the scope
management plan. An alternatives analysis is an example of the data analysis tools and
techniques that can be used in this process.
- **C Create WBS using decomposition**
Incorrect. Decomposition is one of the tools and techniques used in the Create WBS
process. However, the creation of the WBS should be carried out only after a scope
management plan is in place, requirements collected, and scope defined.
- **D Define Scope using interpersonal and team skills**
Incorrect. Various interpersonal and team skills, such as nominal group technique,
observation/conservation, facilitation, can be used while defining the scope of the project.
However, the Define Scope process cannot be performed before the scope management plan
is developed, and requirements collected.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 136, 130
Bottom of Form

Question ID: 651656
Which of the following is a tool or technique of the Conduct Procurements process?
Top of Form
- **A Communication technology**
- **B Project performance appraisals**
- **C Interpersonal and team skills**
- **D Qualified seller list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Negotiating with vendors is required so that mutual agreement can be reached before signing the
contracts.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Conduct Procurements is the process of obtaining seller responses, selecting a seller, and
awarding a contract. The Conduct Procurements process has the following five tools and
techniques:
● Expert judgment
● Advertising
● Bidder conferences
● Data analysis
● Interpersonal and team skills

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communication technology**
Incorrect. Communication technology is a tool and technique used in the Project
Communications Management Knowledge Area. The PMBOK® Guide does not include
communications technology as a tool and technique used in the Conduct Procurements
process.
- **B Project performance appraisals**
Incorrect. Project performance appraisals typically take place during the Develop Team
process and not the Conduct Procurements process.
- **C Interpersonal and team skills**
Correct. The interpersonal and team skill of negotiation is a tool and technique used in the
Conduct Procurements process.
- **D Qualified seller list**
Incorrect. The qualified seller list is an organizational process asset and is an input to the
Conduct Procurements process. It is not a tool or technique.

Filtered Mode: Displaying 210 questions
Question 162 of 210
Question ID: 651672
All of the following are inputs to the Close Project or Phase process except:
Top of Form
- **A Milestone list**
- **B Quality control measurements**
- **C Verified deliverables**
- **D Project communications**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the answers is an input to the Validate Scope process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Close Project or Phase process is where all activities for the project, phase, or contract are
finalized. It has the following eight inputs:
● Project charter
● Project management plan
● Project documents (e.g., milestone list, quality control measurements, project
communications)
● Accepted deliverables
● Business documents
● Agreements
● Procurement documentation
● Organizational process assets

---

Verified deliverables are an input to the Validate Scope process, not the Close Project or Phase
process. Since the question is worded negatively, "All of the following are inputs to the Close
Project or Phase process except", verified deliverables are the correct answer.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Milestone list**
Incorrect. The milestone list shows the final dates on which the project milestones have
been accomplished. Therefore, the milestone list is an input to the Close Project or Phase
process.
- **B Quality control measurements**
Incorrect. The quality control measurements document the results of the Control Quality
activities and demonstrate compliance with the quality requirements. The quality control
measurements are an example of project documents and are inputs to the Close Project or
Phase process.
- **C Verified deliverables**
Correct. Verified deliverables are completed project deliverables that have been checked
and confirmed for correctness through the Control Quality process. Verified deliverables
are inputs to the Validate Scope process. Accepted deliverables are inputs to the Close
Project or Phase process.
- **D Project communications**
Incorrect. Project communications are an example of project documents that serve as input
to the Close Project or Phase process. Project communications include all communications
that have been created throughout the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 121, 124-125
